Defending the Contract: The Status of Khabar Ahad
Baqillani answers the objection that the contract was invalid due to the condition of taqlid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani defends the validity of the contract by challenging the reliability of the opposing report and affirming the integrity of the Companions.

Core Idea
A report of a single chain cannot override the known righteousness of the Companions.

In this passage, Baqillani addresses a historical objection about the contract made by 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf to appoint 'Uthman as caliph. Critics claimed the contract was invalid because it allegedly required 'Uthman to follow the precedents of Abu Bakr and 'Umar, which would constitute forbidden taqlid. Baqillani responds by questioning the authenticity of this report and defending the Companions from such accusations based on uncertain evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the passage carefully, noting the objector's claim and Baqillani's response. The objection is presented first, followed by the answer.
Pay attention to the structure: the objection is introduced with 'If they say...' and the answer with 'It is said to them...'.
2
Identify the two-part response
Baqillani gives two main arguments: (1) the report is a khabar ahad, not known with certainty; (2) the Companions, being more knowledgeable and God-fearing, would not have accepted forbidden taqlid. Find these in the text.
3
Understand the implications for historical criticism
Reflect on why the status of the report matters. Baqillani uses the principle that isolated reports cannot be used to accuse the Sahaba of wrongdoing. Consider how this protects the integrity of the early community.
This connects to broader methodology in kalam: reliance on certain knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قالوا : وكيف يكون عقد عبد الرحمن لعثمان صحيحاً وقد عقد لـه على شرط تقليده في الأحكام لأبي بكر وعمر وما روي عنه من أنه قال لعلي : نبايع لك ونعقد لك هذا الأمر على أن تحكم بكتاب الله وسنة نبيه وسنة الشيخين من بعده (۳) ، وأن علياً قال : ليس مثلي من استظهر عليه ولكن أجتهد رأيي، وأنه عرض ذلك على عثمان فرضي بالشرط وضمِنَهُ وعُقِدَ لـه عليه (٤) وقد اتفقنا على أن التقليد من العالم لغيره حرام في الدين؟ يقال لهم : هذا الخبر أيضاً من أخبار الآحاد وليس هو مما يعلم صحته ضرورة ولا بدليل . فإن كان التقليد حراماً فإن الصحابة قد كانت أعلم بذلك وأتقى الله من أن تدخل في الحرام على غير إنكار له وكان يجب على علي عليه السلام مع من قبول الشرط أن يقول : هذا حرام في الدين لا يحل فعله . وليس لنا أن نطعن على الصحابة بشيء نضيفه إليهم لا نجيزه علينا بـروايــات الأحاد فسقط أيضاً التعلق بهذه الروايات .
And if they say: How can the contract of 'Abd al-Rahman for 'Uthman be valid when he contracted for him on the condition of his following Abu Bakr and 'Umar in legal rulings, and what has been reported from him that he said to 'Ali: 'We give allegiance to you and contract this matter for you on condition that you judge by the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of His Prophet, and the Sunnah of the two shaykhs after him' (3), and that 'Ali said: 'One like me is not to be sought to be prevailed over, but I will exercise my ijtihad,' and that he presented that to 'Uthman, so he accepted the condition and guaranteed it, and the contract was made for him on that basis (4), and we have agreed that taqlid from a scholar to another is forbidden in the religion? It is said to them: This report is also among the khabar ahad and is not known with certainty necessarily or by evidence. For if taqlid is forbidden, then the Companions were more knowledgeable of that and more God-fearing than to enter into the forbidden without rejecting it, and it would have been incumbent upon 'Ali (peace be upon him) when he was asked to accept the condition to say: 'This is forbidden in the religion, it is not permissible to do it.' And it is not for us to criticize the Companions for something we attribute to them that we do not permit for ourselves based on khabar ahad. So attachment to these reports also falls.
Source pages p. 519

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objector questions the validity of 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf's contract with 'Uthman because it allegedly stipulated taqlid of Abu Bakr and 'Umar, which is forbidden. Additionally, 'Ali refused the condition, but 'Uthman accepted. Baqillani's answer is twofold: First, this report is a khabar ahad (isolated report) and not definitively established. Second, if taqlid were truly forbidden, the Companions were more aware and would not have accepted it; 'Ali would have explicitly declared it forbidden. Since we cannot attribute such violations to the Sahaba based on uncertain reports, the objection is invalid.

Key Terms
عقد
شرط
تقليد
خبر آحاد
حرام
صحابة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A single report (khabar ahad) can definitively prove that a Companion committed a sin like forbidden taqlid.
Correction: Baqillani argues that khabar ahad does not provide certainty and cannot be used to accuse the Sahaba of wrongdoing, especially when it contradicts their known piety.

Checkpoint
What is Baqillani's primary response to the objection that the contract with 'Uthman stipulated forbidden taqlid?
A) He accepts that the contract was invalid.
B) He argues that taqlid is not actually forbidden.
C) He says the report is a khabar ahad and thus not reliable.
D) He claims that 'Ali actually accepted the condition.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a historical claim about the Companions cannot be established by isolated reports that contradict their known piety.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever judged someone—perhaps a scholar or a community member—based on a rumor or a single report, without verifying its certainty? How does this lesson about the Companions challenge your willingness to accept such reports today?
?
When you hear a story that casts doubt on the integrity of the early Muslims, do you instinctively trust it or question it? Will you commit to seeking certain knowledge before forming opinions about the righteous?
?
The Companions were more God-fearing than to enter into the forbidden. Is there an area in your life where you rely on weak evidence to justify your actions or judgments? What would it look like to adopt the same caution the Sahaba are presumed to have?

Interpreting the Condition: Justice, Not Taqlid
Baqillani offers an alternative interpretation of the condition as a call for just conduct.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's alternative interpretation of the condition and why he argues it was about justice rather than blind imitation.

Core Idea
The condition was a call for justice, not blind adherence.

Baqillani offers a reconciliatory reading of the historical report. He suggests that 'Abd al-Rahman's stipulation of following the 'Sunnah of the two shaykhs' was actually a call for just conduct, not a demand for taqlid. This interpretation preserves the integrity of all parties and resolves the apparent conflict.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage carefully, then its literal translation. Notice the key terms like 'sunnah of the two shaykhs' and 'conduct with justice'.
2
Understand Baqillani's reinterpretation
Identify how Baqillani reinterprets the condition: he argues it was not about following every specific ruling but about upholding justice and fairness. He also suggests it was meant to affirm 'Ali, not doubt him.
3
Examine the evidence from differing rulings
Note the evidence Baqillani provides: that Abu Bakr and Umar had differing rulings in many matters (e.g., inheritance, stipends), so it would be impossible for Uthman to follow both. This shows the condition must have been about general justice.
4
Reflect on the resolution
Consider how this interpretation resolves the tensions: 'Abd al-Rahman, 'Ali, and 'Uthman are all correct. 'Abd al-Rahman meant justice, 'Ali understood it as taqlid (hence refusal), and 'Uthman accepted it as a call to justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويمكن أيضاً، إن كانت هذه الرواية صحيحة، ألا يكون عبد الرحمن أراد بسنة الشيخين اتباعهما على التقليد في الأحكام وإنما أراد السيرة بالعدل والإنصاف وألا يكون قال ذلك أيضاً على شك منه في أن علياً سيحكم بالإنصاف والعدل إن صار الأمر إليه وإنما قال ذلك على مذهب التقرير لـه والتأكيد والتبرئة له ليقع الرضا من الجماعة وتزول الفتنة ويستميل بذلك قلوب السامعين له فيكون عبد الرحمن مصيباً في اشتراطه وتقريره وتأكيد الأمر ويكون علي مصيباً في الامتناع منه ويكون عثمان مصيباً أيضاً في قبول الاشتراط لما أن عبد الرحمن ما قصد إلا التأكيد والتقرير واشتراط السيرة بالعدل. من ويدل على ذلك ويؤكده علمنا وعلم سائر الناس أن أحكام أبي بكر وعمر في كثير من الفقهيات مختلفة كتوريث الجد والمفاضلة في العطاء من عمر وتسوية أبي بكر بين الناس فيه وغير ذلك ؛ وأن عثمان لا يمكنه ولا يجوز أن يحكم بحكميهما المختلفين ؛ فدل ذلك على أنه إنما أراد اشتراط السيرة بالعدل والإنصاف .
And it is also possible, if this report is authentic, that 'Abd al-Rahman did not intend by the 'Sunnah of the two shaykhs' to follow them in taqlid in legal rulings, but rather he intended the conduct of justice and fairness; and that he also did not say that out of doubt that 'Ali would rule with fairness and justice if the matter came to him, but rather he said that in the manner of affirming him, emphasizing, and exonerating him so that satisfaction would occur from the group and discord would disappear, and by that he would attract the hearts of the listeners to him. So 'Abd al-Rahman would be correct in his stipulation, affirmation, and emphasis of the matter, and 'Ali would be correct in his refusal of it, and 'Uthman would also be correct in accepting the stipulation, because 'Abd al-Rahman intended only affirmation and emphasis and stipulating conduct with justice. What indicates and confirms that is our knowledge and the knowledge of all people that the rulings of Abu Bakr and 'Umar in many jurisprudential matters differed, like the inheritance of the grandfather and the differentiation in stipends by 'Umar and the equalization by Abu Bakr among people in that, and other things; and that 'Uthman cannot and it is not permissible for him to judge by both their different rulings. So that indicated that he only intended to stipulate conduct with justice and fairness.
Source pages p. 520

Commentary
This passage is an alternative interpretation. Baqillani proposes that even if the report is authentic, the condition of following the sunnah of the two shaykhs likely meant adhering to justice and fairness, not blind imitation in legal rulings. He suggests 'Abd al-Rahman may have said this to calm the community and remove discord, not because he doubted 'Ali's justice. Consequently, all three figures were correct: 'Abd al-Rahman in his intention of justice, 'Ali in refusing (as he understood it as taqlid), and 'Uthman in accepting (since he understood it as a call to justice). The evidence is that the rulings of Abu Bakr and 'Umar often differed, so 'Uthman could not have followed both; therefore, the condition must have been about justice.

Key Terms
سنة الشيخين
سيرة بالعدل
تقرير
تأكيد
فتنة
اجتهاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The condition meant that the caliph must follow every specific ruling of Abu Bakr and Umar without exception.
Correction: Baqillani argues that the condition was about upholding justice and fairness, not blind adherence to all their rulings, as evidenced by their differing decisions.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani's alternative interpretation, what did 'Abd al-Rahman actually intend by 'Sunnah of the two shaykhs'?
A) To follow their every legal ruling.
B) To imitate them blindly in all matters.
C) To conduct affairs with justice and fairness.
D) To appoint 'Ali as caliph.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani's reinterpretation shows that the condition was about justice, not taqlid, thus reconciling the actions of all involved.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever judged someone's action as wrong when you didn't know their true intention? How would Bāqillānī's approach of giving the best possible interpretation change the way you interact with others? Commit to applying this to a specific person this week.
?
Bāqillānī argued that differing rulings of Abu Bakr and 'Umar prove the condition was about justice, not blind following. Are there teachings or leaders you follow without considering the underlying principle of justice? What would it mean for you to prioritize justice over mere conformity?
?
When you face a conflict where both sides claim to follow the 'right way,' do you seek to reconcile like Bāqillānī did, or do you take sides? How might your faith deepen if you worked to understand each party's perspective instead of rushing to judgment?

Another Interpretation: The Condition Could Not Be Taqlid
Baqillani argues against the taqlid interpretation using the practice of the two shaykhs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani argues that the condition in the shura story could not have been about taqlid, based on the practice of the two shaykhs.

Core Idea
The two shaykhs' practice of ijtihad disproves the taqlid interpretation.

Baqillani offers a second interpretation of the condition in the shura story. He argues that 'Abd al-Rahman could not have called 'Uthman to taqlid because Abu Bakr and 'Umar themselves rejected taqlid and practiced ijtihad. This passage shows how historical precedent is used in theological argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay attention to how Baqillani structures his argument with a conditional premise.
The passage begins with 'وقد يمكن أيضاً' signaling an alternative interpretation.
2
Identify the key premise
Baqillani's key premise is the known practice (sira) of Abu Bakr and 'Umar: they rejected taqlid and exercised ijtihad, even differing from each other in legal rulings.
He cites specific examples: 'Umar did not imitate Abu Bakr, nor did Abu Bakr imitate 'Umar.
3
Understand the inference
If the condition had been about taqlid, it would contradict the sira of the two shaykhs, which 'Abd al-Rahman would not do. Therefore, the condition must be about something else (as argued earlier).
Baqillani concludes that the condition concerned justice, not taqlid.
4
Note the role of 'Ali
'Ali misunderstood the condition as a call to taqlid, and while his refusal was correct, his reason was mistaken. This nuance strengthens Baqillani's overall case.
The passage ends with 'Ali's correct refusal but for the wrong reason.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد يمكن أيضاً إن كانت هذه الرواية ألا يكون عبد الرحمن اشترط على عثمان ترك التقليد في الأحكام لأن سيرة أبي بكر وعمر ترك التقليد فيهما والنهي عن ذلك. فذلك لم يُقَلّد عمر أبا بكر بل خالفه ولا قلد أبو بكر عمر في شيء من مسائل الحلال والحرام، وقد علم من سيرتهما اجتهاد الإمام وترك التقليد لغيره فكيف يدعوه عبد الرحمن إلى التقليد وترك الاجتهاد وهذا وهذا ضد سنتهما؟ فبان أنه لم يدعه إلا إلى ما ذكرناه وأن علياً قدَّرَ فيه أنه دعاه إلى التقليد فأصاب في امتناعه من قبـول الشرط.
And it is also possible, if this report is authentic, that 'Abd al-Rahman did not stipulate on 'Uthman the abandonment of ijtihad in legal rulings, because the practice (sira) of Abu Bakr and 'Umar was the abandonment of taqlid and the prohibition of that. For that reason, 'Umar did not imitate Abu Bakr but rather opposed him, nor did Abu Bakr imitate 'Umar in anything from the matters of halal and haram. And it is known from their practice the ijtihad of the Imam and the abandonment of taqlid for others. So how could 'Abd al-Rahman call him to taqlid and abandonment of ijtihad, and this and this are contrary to their practice? So it became clear that he only called him to what we have mentioned, and that 'Ali estimated that he had called him to taqlid, so he was correct in his refusal to accept the condition.
Source pages p. 520

Commentary
This passage is another interpretation. Baqillani argues that it is also possible that 'Abd al-Rahman did not stipulate taqlid at all, because the known practice (sira) of Abu Bakr and 'Umar was to reject taqlid and engage in ijtihad. They did not imitate each other; 'Umar differed from Abu Bakr, and Abu Bakr did not imitate 'Umar. Therefore, it would be inconsistent for 'Abd al-Rahman to call Uthman to something the two shaykhs themselves opposed. Thus, the condition must have been about what was mentioned earlier (justice). 'Ali misunderstood it as a call to taqlid, so his refusal was correct.

Key Terms
سيرة
اجتهاد
تقليد
خلاف
إمام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the condition in the shura story was about taqlid and that Baqillani agrees with 'Ali's reason for refusal.
Correction: Baqillani argues the condition was not about taqlid; 'Ali misunderstood it as taqlid, but Baqillani still affirms his refusal was correct because the condition (about justice) was unacceptable to him.

Checkpoint
Why does Baqillani think 'Abd al-Rahman could not have stipulated taqlid?
A) Because 'Abd al-Rahman was opposed to taqlid personally.
B) Because the practice of Abu Bakr and 'Umar was to reject taqlid and practice ijtihad.
C) Because 'Uthman refused to accept taqlid.
D) Because 'Ali had already rejected it.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani uses the historical practice of the two shaykhs to argue that the condition in the shura story could not have been about taqlid, thereby defending the interpretation that it concerned the requirement of justice in the caliph.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you follow a scholar or a teacher, do you do it blindly (taqlid) or do you try to understand the evidence and reasoning? What is one area of your life where you might be imitating others without checking the truth, and will you commit to seeking the evidence this week?
?
The two shaykhs disagreed with each other in rulings but remained united. Is there a person you disagree with (in your family, community, or masjid) where you have let disagreement lead to disunity? Will you work to maintain brotherhood despite differences, just as Abu Bakr and 'Umar did?
?
Imagine you are in 'Ali's position: you reject a condition because you think it is wrong (taqlid), but later you realize it was about justice. Are you humble enough to admit you misunderstood? When have you rejected something based on an assumption, and how can you train yourself to seek clarification first?

Defending the Companions: Justice, Not Taqlid
Baqillani argues that the condition of following the two shaykhs means justice, not taqlid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument that the condition of following the two shaykhs in the consultation was about justice and fairness, not blind imitation, and that this interpretation protects the Companions from accusations of sin.

Core Idea
Following the two shaykhs means justice, not blind imitation.

In the famous consultation after Umar's death, Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf stipulated that the next caliph must follow the sunna of the two shaykhs (Abu Bakr and Umar). This condition has been used by some to accuse Ali of reluctance or to imply that the Companions committed sin. But is that fair? Baqillani offers a careful defense, arguing that the condition was about upholding justice, not about blindly copying every ruling.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Let the author's argument come through before analyzing.
The passage is dense; read slowly.
2
Identify the key claim against accusations
Notice where Baqillani says we cannot attack the Companions based on weak reports. This is his first defense.
3
Understand the charitable interpretation
Find where Baqillani reinterprets 'sunna of the two shaykhs' as conduct of justice and fairness, not taqlid.
4
See the evidence from differing rulings
Look at the examples of Abu Bakr and Umar differing in inheritance and stipends. This shows impossible to follow both literally.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Notice that Baqillani concludes all three Companions were correct in their actions, preserving their integrity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
امتناعه تدخل في الحرام على غير إنكار له وكان يجب على علي عليه السلام مع من قبول الشرط أن يقول : هذا حرام في الدين لا يحل فعله . وليس لنا أن نطعن على الصحابة بشيء نضيفه إليهم لا نجيزه علينا بروايات الأحاديث فسقط أيضاً التعلق بهذه الروايات . ويمكن أيضاً، إن كانت هذه الرواية صحيحة، ألا يكون عبد الرحمن أراد بسنة الشيخين اتباعهما على التقليد في الأحكام وإنما أراد السيرة بالعدل والإنصاف وألا يكون قال ذلك أيضاً على شك منه في أن علياً سيحكم بالإنصاف والعدل إن صار الأمر إليه وإنما قال ذلك على مذهب التقرير له والتأكيد والتبرئة له ليقع الرضا من الجماعة وتزول الفتنة ويستميل بذلك قلوب السامعين له فيكون عبد الرحمن مصيباً في اشتراطه وتقريره وتأكيد الأمر ويكون علي مصيباً في الامتناع منه ويكون عثمان مصيباً أيضاً في قبول الاشتراط لما أن عبد الرحمن ما قصد إلا التأكيد والتقرير واشتراط السيرة بالعدل. ويدل على ذلك ويؤكده علمنا وعلم سائر الناس أن أحكام أبي بكر وعمر في كثير من الفقهيات مختلفة كتوريث الجد والمفاضلة في العطاء من عمر وتسوية أبي بكر بين الناس فيه وغير ذلك ؛ وأن عثمان لا يمكنه ولا يجوز أن يحكم بحكميهما المختلفين ؛ فدل ذلك على أنه إنما أراد اشتراط السيرة بالعدل والإنصاف .
His refusal enters into the forbidden without his having denied it, and it was incumbent upon Ali, peace be upon him, with whoever accepted the condition to say: This is forbidden in the religion, it is not permissible to do it. And it is not for us to attack the Companions with something we attribute to them that we do not permit for ourselves through reports of hadiths, so the reliance on these reports also falls away. And it is also possible, if this report is authentic, that Abd al-Rahman did not intend by 'the sunna of the two shaykhs' to follow them through taqlid in rulings, but rather intended the conduct of justice and fairness; and that he did not say that out of doubt that Ali would rule with justice and fairness if the matter came to him, but rather he said it as a way of affirming him, emphasizing him, and absolving him, so that the group would be pleased, the tribulation would cease, and he would thereby win the hearts of those listening to him. Thus Abd al-Rahman was correct in his condition, his affirmation, and his emphasis; and Ali was correct in refraining from it; and Uthman was also correct in accepting the condition, because Abd al-Rahman intended nothing except emphasis, affirmation, and stipulating conduct with justice. And what indicates and confirms that is our knowledge and the knowledge of all people that the rulings of Abu Bakr and Umar in many jurisprudential matters differed, such as the inheritance of the grandfather, the differentiation in stipends by Umar, and Abu Bakr's equalization among people in that, and other than that; and that Uthman could not and may not rule according to both of their different rulings. So that indicated that he only intended stipulating conduct with justice and fairness.
Source pages p. 520

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the Companions against accusations of wrongdoing in the story of the consultation after Umar's death. The author begins by addressing the issue of Ali's refusal to accept the condition of following the sunna of Abu Bakr and Umar. He argues that if Ali had considered the condition sinful, he would have explicitly said so. Since he did not, we cannot attribute sin to the Companions based on weak narrations. Then, assuming the report is authentic, the author presents a charitable interpretation: Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf did not mean blind imitation (taqlid) of the two shaykhs in all rulings, but rather intended to stipulate that the caliph should follow the path of justice and fairness, which was their general practice. He likely said this to reassure the community, not out of doubt about Ali. Thus all three—Abd al-Rahman, Ali, and Uthman—were correct in their actions. The author supports this by noting that Abu Bakr and Umar themselves differed on many legal rulings, so it would be impossible for Uthman to follow both simultaneously. This proves the condition was about general justice, not specific imitation.

Key Terms
سنة الشيخين
التقليد
السيرة بالعدل والإنصاف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the condition of following the two shaykhs was a demand for blind imitation (taqlid) of all their specific rulings, implying that Ali's reluctance was sinful.
Correction: Baqillani argues it was a condition for justice and fairness, not taqlid, as shown by the inevitable differences in their rulings.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what did Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf actually intend by his condition of following the sunna of the two shaykhs?
A) Blind imitation (taqlid) of all their specific rulings
B) Conducting affairs with justice and fairness, following their general example
C) Rejecting Ali's caliphate outright
D) Forcing Uthman to accept all their rulings without exception

Key Takeaway
Baqillani defends the Companions by showing that the condition of following the two shaykhs was a call to justice, not blind imitation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear about disagreements among early Muslims, do you rush to judge one side, or do you follow Baqillani's example of seeking the best interpretation? Will you commit to withholding judgment until you can find a charitable explanation, just as he did for Abd al-Rahman, Ali, and Uthman?
?
This lesson shows that even in a tense political moment, the Companions acted with justice and wisdom. How often do you assume the worst about others in debates within your family or community? Will you actively stop yourself from attributing bad intentions and instead look for the best possible motive?
?
Baqillani uses the fact that Abu Bakr and Umar differed to prove the condition was about general justice. When you see differences among scholars today, do you use them to dismiss the tradition entirely, or do you see them as evidence of a higher principle? Confront your own tendency to use disagreements as an excuse to ignore the path of justice.

Ali's Refusal as Valid Ijtihad
Baqillani presents a second possibility regarding the condition's meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's second interpretation of the condition imposed on Uthman and why Ali's refusal was considered a valid ijtihad, not a condemnation.

Core Idea
Ali's refusal was a valid difference of ijtihad, not a condemnation.

Baqillani offers a second possibility: the condition was not about taqlid but about something else. He argues that since Abu Bakr and Umar themselves practiced ijtihad and avoided taqlid, Abd al-Rahman could not have intended taqlid. Ali, however, understood it as taqlid and refused, which was correct from his perspective. This lesson examines the reasoning behind this interpretation and its implications for understanding early Islamic disputes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Let the flow of Baqillani's argument settle in your mind.
Pay attention to the conditional phrase 'if this report [is authentic]'.
2
Identify the key evidence
Notice how Baqillani uses the conduct of Abu Bakr and Umar—how they did not imitate each other—to argue that Abd al-Rahman could not have intended taqlid.
This is the core of the argument.
3
Understand the conclusion about Ali
Recognize that Baqillani concludes Ali's refusal was correct from his perspective because he saw the condition as calling to taqlid, which he believed was impermissible.
This shows that both actors were correct in their own ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد يمكن أيضاً إن كانت هذه الرواية ألا يكون عبد الرحمن اشترط على عثمان ترك التقليد في الأحكام لأن سيرة أبي بكر وعمر ترك التقليد فيهما والنهي عن ذلك. فذلك لم يُقَلّد عمر أبا بكر بل خالفه ولا قلد أبو بكر عمر في شيء من مسائل الحلال والحرام، وقد علم من سيرتهما اجتهاد الإمام وترك التقليد لغيره فكيف يدعوه عبد الرحمن إلى التقليد وترك الاجتهاد وهذا وهذا ضد سنتهما؟ فبان أنه لم يدعه إلا إلى ما ذكرناه وأن علياً قدَّرَ فيه أنه دعاه إلى التقليد فأصاب في امتناعه من قبول أن الشرط.
And it is also possible, if this report [is authentic], that Abd al-Rahman did not stipulate to Uthman the abandonment of taqlid in rulings, because the conduct of Abu Bakr and Umar was the abandonment of taqlid in them and the prohibition of that. So Umar did not imitate Abu Bakr but rather differed from him, nor did Abu Bakr imitate Umar in any matter of the lawful and the forbidden. And it is known from their conduct the ijtihad of the imam and the abandonment of taqlid of others. So how could Abd al-Rahman call him to taqlid and the abandonment of ijtihad, and this is contrary to their sunna? So it became clear that he only called him to what we mentioned, and that Ali estimated that he called him to taqlid, so he was correct in his refusal to accept the condition.
Source pages p. 520

Commentary
In this passage, Baqillani offers a second interpretative possibility regarding the condition of following the two shaykhs. He argues that Abd al-Rahman did not stipulate taqlid because the practice of Abu Bakr and Umar themselves was to avoid taqlid and exercise independent judgment (ijtihad). For example, Umar did not imitate Abu Bakr when he differed on issues like inheritance and stipends. Therefore, it would be inconsistent for Abd al-Rahman to demand taqlid. Instead, the condition must have been about something else, likely justice as previously mentioned. Ali, however, understood the condition as a call to taqlid, which he rejected because his own view was that taqlid is not permissible. Thus, Ali was correct in his refusal from his perspective, and Abd al-Rahman was correct in his intention. This shows that both acted according to their own valid ijtihad, and no blame attaches to either.

Key Terms
التقليد
الاجتهاد
سيرة أبي بكر وعمر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Ali's refusal implies he condemned Abd al-Rahman's action as sinful or that he believed the condition was inherently wrong.
Correction: Baqillani clarifies that Ali's refusal was based on his own ijtihad, not a condemnation. He acted correctly according to his understanding, and Abd al-Rahman also acted correctly.

Checkpoint
Why does Baqillani argue that Abd al-Rahman could not have intended taqlid?
A) Because the two shaykhs themselves practiced taqlid
B) Because the two shaykhs abandoned taqlid and practiced ijtihad
C) Because Uthman was a mujtahid and didn't need to follow anyone
D) Because Ali had explicitly forbidden taqlid

Key Takeaway
Baqillani shows that both Abd al-Rahman and Ali acted according to valid ijtihad, with no blame on either.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you disagree with a leader or scholar, do you immediately assume they are wrong, or do you consider the possibility that they too may be exercising valid ijtihad? How does this lesson challenge your tendency to condemn differences?
?
Are you willing to accept that someone may sincerely hold a different view based on their own ijtihad, even if you believe it is mistaken? What would it take for you to treat them with the same respect Baqillani shows Ali and Abd al-Rahman?
?
Have you ever used the excuse of 'ijtihad' to justify refusing to follow a ruling when the real reason was laziness or desire? How can you ensure your reasoning is sincere and not a cover for disobedience?

Permissibility of Taqlid Among Scholars
Baqillani argues for the permissibility of taqlid among scholars as a valid difference of opinion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the permissibility of a scholar imitating another scholar (taqlid) as a valid matter of ijtihad to defend the actions of Uthman and Abd al-Rahman in the contract dispute with Ali.

Core Idea
Taqlid among scholars is a valid difference of opinion, not a sin.

In this passage, Baqillani introduces a third defense: that some scholars permit one scholar to imitate another in rulings. This is a matter of ijtihad, meaning there is room for valid disagreement. He applies this to the case of Uthman and Abd al-Rahman, suggesting that they held the permissibility of taqlid, while Ali did not. Thus, both parties acted within their own ijtihad, and no blame attaches.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the translation. Let Baqillani's argument emerge naturally.
Notice the phrase 'وهي مسألة اجتهاد' — this is the key point.
2
Identify the claim and its basis
Baqillani cites that some jurists hold taqlid among scholars as permissible. He then qualifies it as a matter of ijtihad. Consider what that implies about the validity of differing views.
3
Apply the claim to the historical case
Baqillani suggests that Uthman and Abd al-Rahman may have held the permissibility of taqlid, while Ali held the opposite. According to Baqillani, each was correct in their own ijtihad.
4
Understand the conclusion
The conclusion is that the contract is not impugned because each party acted according to their own valid ijtihad. This removes the opponents' objection.
Note that Baqillani does not require Uthman and Abd al-Rahman to follow Ali's view, even if taqlid is permissible for them.
5
Reflect on the broader lesson
Consider how Baqillani uses the concept of ijtihad to accommodate differences among the Companions, defending them against criticism.
This reflects a key kalam method: resolving historical disputes through legal theory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد قال قوم من الفقهاء إن تقليد العالم للعالم والحكم بالتقليد جائز سائغ في الدين وهي مسألة اجتهاد أعني تقليد العالم للعالم فلعل عثمان وعبد الرحمن كانا يريان جواز التقليد والحُكْمَ به وعلي عليه السلام لا يرى ذلك فأصابا فيما تعاقدا عليه وأصاب علي في امتناعه من غير قدح في العقد لأنه لا يحرم ذلك على من رآه وإن وجب عليه ألا يفعله لأنه ليس من رأيه واجتهاده. فبان بذلك أجمعَ زوالُ ما تعلقوا به في هذا الفصل.
And some jurists have said that the imitation (taqlid) of a scholar by a scholar and judging by taqlid is permissible and legitimate in the religion, and it is a matter of ijtihad—I mean the imitation of a scholar by a scholar. So perhaps Uthman and Abd al-Rahman held the permissibility of taqlid and judging by it, while Ali, peace be upon him, did not hold that. So both were correct in what they agreed upon, and Ali was correct in his refusal, without any disparagement of the contract, because he does not deem that forbidden for one who holds it, even though it was incumbent upon him not to do it because it was not his opinion and ijtihad. So by all that, the removal of what they clung to in this chapter became clear.
Source pages p. 521

Commentary
In this passage, Baqillani introduces a third argument based on the permissibility of taqlid for a scholar. He notes that some jurists allow a scholar to imitate another scholar in rulings, and this is a matter of ijtihad—meaning there is valid difference of opinion. Therefore, it is possible that Uthman and Abd al-Rahman held the view that taqlid is permissible, while Ali held that it is not. Each acted according to their own ijtihad. Thus, Uthman and Abd al-Rahman were correct in their agreement (the contract), and Ali was correct in his refusal, all without disparaging the contract. This is because a person is not required to do what is against his own ijtihad, even if the other view is permissible. So all accusations based on this incident collapse.

Key Terms
تقليد العالم للعالم
مسألة اجتهاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if taqlid is wrong, then Uthman and Abd al-Rahman sinned.
Correction: Baqillani shows that taqlid among scholars is a valid difference of opinion (mas'alah ijtihad), so each party acted correctly according to their own view, and no sin occurred.

Checkpoint
What is the significance of the statement that taqlid of a scholar by a scholar is a matter of ijtihad?
A) It means taqlid is obligatory
B) It means there is a valid difference of opinion, so both parties can be correct
C) It means Ali was wrong to refuse
D) It means the contract was invalid

Key Takeaway
Baqillani uses the permissibility of taqlid among scholars as a valid matter of ijtihad to show that Uthman, Abd al-Rahman, and Ali each acted correctly according to their own views, thus defending the contract.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a disagreement between scholars on a matter, do you automatically dismiss one side as wrong, or do you recognize it as a valid difference of ijtihad? How does Baqillani's argument challenge your instinct to judge?
?
Have you ever refused to follow a ruling because it was not your own opinion, even when it was permissible? What prevented you from accepting it, and how does this lesson call you to humility?
?
Think of a time you criticized someone for following a scholar you disagreed with. Can you now see that person as acting according to their own ijtihad? Will you change how you speak about such differences from today?

Refuting Objections Against Abd al-Rahman and Uthman
Objection-and-answer: Baqillani refutes the Shi'a argument and defends the stability of imamate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's refutation of the objection that Abd al-Rahman's later denunciation invalidates Uthman's imamate, and the principle that a validly contracted imamate is not undone by subsequent words or accusations.

Core Idea
A valid imamate is not invalidated by later statements.

This passage addresses a key Shi'a objection: that Abd al-Rahman's alleged later criticism of Uthman proves his initial contract was invalid. Baqillani responds by dismissing the reports as fabricated and, more importantly, establishing the principle that once the imamate is validly contracted, it cannot be overturned by the contracting party's later words or by anyone's censure. The only way an imam is removed is through clear manifest events, not mere accusations.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
First, read the Arabic passage and translation. Note the objection: that Abd al-Rahman's later statements show his contract was wrong.
The objectors cite reports of Abd al-Rahman calling Uthman a tyrant and even calling for his removal.
2
Identify the first response
Baqillani's first move is to dismiss the reports as fabricated, pointing to the established historical record of Abd al-Rahman's satisfaction.
He says 'this too is among the fabricated reports' and gives evidence of Abd al-Rahman's public approval.
3
Grasp the second response: principle of imamate stability
Even if the reports were true, Baqillani argues that a valid imamate is not removed by the contracting party's later withdrawal or anyone's censure. This is a key doctrinal point.
The imamate is established by a valid contract; later words cannot undo it.
4
Understand the criterion for removal
Baqillani explains that an imam is only removed by clear, manifest, established events (like open sin or incapacity). Mere accusations or misinterpretations do not suffice.
He says we must examine the specific grievances; if they are baseless, we disregard them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : كيف يكون عقد عبد الرحمن صحيحاً، وهو قد أنكر على عثمان ونقم كثيراً من أفعاله وقال للصحابة لما قال له بعضهم: هذا من عملك، حيث عقدت لهذا الظالم الجبار ، فقال لهم : ما علمت وإذا شئتم أخذت سيفي على عاتقي وأخذتم أسيافكم وقتلنا هذا الطاغية وأزلناه عن الأمر»، ونحو ذلك؟ يقال لهم : هذا أيضاً من الروايات المختلقة لأن الثابت المعلوم من حال عبد الرحمن رضاه به واختياره له وقوله خطيباً بذلك: «إني رأيت الناس لا يعدلون بعثمان أحداً فولَّيْتُه» في نظائر لهذه الروايات مما يقتضى موالاة عبد الرحمن لعثمان فلا وجه لترك ذلك والتعلق بالتعاليل والأباطيل . على أنه لو صح عن عبد الرحمن أنه قال: «إني خلعت عثمان فاقتلوا هذا الطاغية أو سيروا لخلعه»، لم ينخلع عثمان لهذا القول من عبد الرحمن ولا من غيره ؛ لأن الإمامة إذا ثبتت بعقد صحيح مأذون فيه لم ينخلع صاحبها بخلع العاقد له بعد ذلك ولا بخلع غيره ولا بذم أحد له ولا ينخلع بالقرف ولا بالتأويل عليه ؛ وإنما ينخلع بالجلي المعلوم من الأحداث الثابتة الظاهرة. فيجب أن ننظر فيما أنكره عبد الرحمن بعد عقده وما نقمه القوم عليه ؛ فإن كان ما يوجب خلع الولاية وسقوط الطاعة صرنا إليه وطالبناه بموجبه وإن كان غلطاً في التأويل وقرفاً بالباطل أضربنا عنه ولم نَحْفَلْ به . فإن لم تقنع الشَّيعة وأبت إلا إبطال إمامة عثمان بهذا التأويل والروايات (1) أخرج الطبري في تاريخه 297/3 عن عمرو بن ميمون الأودي أن عبد الرحمن قال يا علي لا تجعل على نفسك سبيلاً فإني قد نظرت وشاورت الناس فإذا هم لا يعدلون بعثمان . 517
If they say: How can the contract of Abd al-Rahman be valid when he objected to Uthman and criticized many of his actions and said to the Companions when one of them said to him: 'This is your doing, since you contracted for this unjust tyrant,' so he said to them: 'I did not know. If you wish, I will take my sword on my shoulder and you take your swords and we will kill this tyrant and remove him from authority,' and similar statements? It is said to them: This too is among the fabricated reports, because what is established and known of Abd al-Rahman's state is his approval of him, his choice of him, and his saying as a speaker: 'I saw that the people do not consider anyone equal to Uthman, so I gave him the caliphate'—in similar reports that indicate Abd al-Rahman's loyalty to Uthman. So there is no reason to abandon that and cling to false pretexts and falsehoods. Moreover, even if it were authentic that Abd al-Rahman said, 'I have removed Uthman, so kill this tyrant or work to remove him,' Uthman would not be removed by this statement from Abd al-Rahman or from anyone else, because when the imamate is established by a valid contract that is permitted, its holder is not removed by the removal of the contracting party afterward, nor by the removal of anyone else, nor by anyone's censure, nor is he removed by false accusation or misinterpretation. Rather, he is only removed by clear known matters of established manifest events. So we must consider what Abd al-Rahman objected to after his contract and what the people criticized him for. If it is something that necessitates removal of authority and the fall of obedience, we would proceed to that and demand its requirement. If it is a mistake in interpretation and a false accusation, we would disregard it and not pay attention to it. If the Shi'a are not satisfied and insist only on invalidating Uthman's imamate through this interpretation and the reports—(1) Al-Tabari narrated in his History 3/297 from Amr ibn Maymun al-Awdi that Abd al-Rahman said: 'O Ali, do not put a way against yourself, for I have looked and consulted the people, and they do not consider anyone equal to Uthman.' 517
Source pages p. 521

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer pair. The objectors (likely Shi'a) question the validity of Abd al-Rahman's contract (i.e., his selection of Uthman) by citing reports that Abd al-Rahman later criticized Uthman, called him a tyrant, and even allegedly encouraged killing him. Baqillani responds with multiple points. First, he dismisses these as fabricated reports, because the established historical fact is that Abd al-Rahman was satisfied with Uthman, chose him, and publicly stated that the people considered no one equal to Uthman—indicating loyalty. So such contradictory reports should be rejected. Second, even if those reports were authentic, Abd al-Rahman's later words would not invalidate Uthman's imamate. Baqillani explains the principle: once the imamate is validly contracted, it cannot be undone by the contracting party's later withdrawal or by anyone's accusation. The imam is only removed by clear, manifest, and established events (like open sin or incapacity). Therefore, we must examine the specific grievances against Uthman: if they merit removal, we would act; if they are false accusations or misinterpretations, we ignore them. Finally, he notes that if the Shi'a remain unconvinced and insist on rejecting Uthman's imamate based on such weak evidence, the argument has been sufficiently refuted.

Key Terms
عقد عبد الرحمن
خلع الإمام
الأحداث الثابتة الظاهرة
الروايات المختلقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Abd al-Rahman's later statements prove his initial contract was invalid.
Correction: Baqillani shows that even if the statements were authentic, they do not invalidate the imamate because a valid contract is not undone by later words.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what is required for an imam to be removed from office after a valid contract?
A) The contracting party's withdrawal
B) Censure by any notable Companion
C) Clear and manifest established events
D) False accusation or misinterpretation

Key Takeaway
A validly contracted imamate is stable and not undone by later statements or accusations; removal requires clear manifest events.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you revoked a commitment because of later hearsay? What does this passage teach you about the stability of a valid contract?
?
Are you quick to accept accusations against others without manifest evidence? How does the principle of 'only removal by clear manifest events' apply to your judgments?
?
If you were in Abd al-Rahman's position, would you stand by your initial choice even when criticized? What would that require of you?

Refuting Allegations of Abd al-Rahman's Regret
Baqillani dismisses the claim that Abd al-Rahman regretted his contract as fabricated narration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes a Shiite claim about Abd al-Rahman's alleged regret, using the dichotomy of fabricated narrations versus established historical facts.

Core Idea
Fabricated narrations cannot override established historical facts.

This lesson deals with a specific historical objection regarding the caliphate of Uthman. The Shiite objection claims that Abd al-Rahman, who was part of the consultative committee, later regretted his choice and called Uthman a tyrant. Baqillani dismisses this as fabricated and points to the established fact of Abd al-Rahman's loyalty.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Shiite claim and the alleged statement of Abd al-Rahman to understand what is being argued.
The objection uses dramatic language about taking up swords.
2
Identify Baqillani's two-part answer
Notice that Baqillani first labels the narration as fabricated, then presents the established fact of Abd al-Rahman's satisfaction.
3
Reflect on the methodology
Consider why Baqillani prioritizes the well-known historical fact over isolated reports. This is a key principle in dealing with historical claims.
This method is common in defending the actions of the Companions.
4
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to confirm you grasped the main point of the refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : كيف يكون عقد عبد الرحمن صحيحاً، وهو قد أنكر على عثمان ونقم كثيراً من أفعاله وقال للصحابة لما قال له بعضهم: هذا من عملك، حيث عقدت لهذا الظالم الجبار ، فقال لهم : ما علمت وإذا شئتم أخذت سيفي على عاتقي وأخذتم أسيافكم وقتلنا هذا الطاغية وأزلناه عن الأمر، ونحو ذلك؟ يقال لهم : هذا أيضاً من الروايات المختلقة لأن الثابت المعلوم من حال عبد الرحمن رضاه به واختياره له وقوله خطيباً بذلك: إني رأيت الناس لا يعدلون بعثمان أحداً فوليته في نظائر لهذه الروايات مما يقتضى موالاة عبد الرحمن لعثمان فلا وجه لترك ذلك والتعلق بالتعاليل والأباطيل .
If they say: 'How can Abd al-Rahman's contract be sound when he criticized Uthman and disapproved of many of his actions, and said to the Companions when some of them said to him: "This is your doing, since you contracted for this unjust tyrant"; he said to them: "I did not know; and if you wish, I will take my sword on my shoulder and you take your swords, and we will kill this tyrant and remove him from authority" and similar?' It is said to them: This too is among the fabricated narrations, because the established and known fact about Abd al-Rahman is his satisfaction with him (Uthman) and his choice of him, and his statement as a preacher: 'I saw that the people consider none equal to Uthman, so I appointed him' – and similar narrations indicate Abd al-Rahman's loyalty to Uthman. So there is no justification to abandon that and cling to baseless statements and falsehoods.
Source pages p. 521

Commentary
This passage presents a Shiite objection and its answer. The objection claims that Abd al-Rahman later regretted his choice and even called Uthman a tyrant. Baqillani's answer is twofold: first, such narrations are fabricated; second, the historically established fact is that Abd al-Rahman was pleased with Uthman, as demonstrated by his own public statement. Therefore, the objection is groundless.

Key Terms
روايات مختلقة (fabricated narrations)
ثابت معلوم (established known fact)
موالاة (loyalty)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That later criticisms by Abd al-Rahman, even if true, would retroactively invalidate the contract.
Correction: Baqillani argues that the narrations of criticism are not even true; they are fabricated.

Checkpoint

A) He was displeased and wanted to depose him
B) He was satisfied and chose him
C) He was neutral
D) He regretted his choice

Key Takeaway
Baqillani refutes the Shiite objection by dismissing the narration as fabricated and affirming the established fact of Abd al-Rahman's satisfaction with Uthman.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a negative story about someone you know, do you instinctively believe it or do you weigh it against their consistent character? This lesson challenges you to treat reports about others with the same rigor—will you commit to verifying information before changing your view of a person?
?
Baqillani dismissed a narration as fabricated because it contradicted established fact. Is there a person you have judged based on a single incident or rumor, ignoring years of known good conduct? How can you correct that injustice today?
?
Abd al-Rahman's public statement shows he acted based on the people's consensus. In your own life, do you seek out the 'established known fact' about a situation, or do you let isolated, emotionally charged stories shape your decisions? What step will you take this week to base your judgments on reliable evidence?

The Shiite Argument Recoils: Similar Narrations Would Invalidate Ali's Caliphate
Baqillani argues that if weak narrations are accepted, then Ali's imamate is even more vulnerable.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani argues that accepting weak narrations against Uthman's caliphate would logically also undermine Ali's imamate, exposing a self-contradiction in the Shiite position.

Core Idea
If weak narrations can invalidate one caliphate, they can invalidate another.

This passage presents a powerful rebuttal from Imam Baqillani. He takes the Shiites' own method of using unverified narrations to attack Uthman's caliphate and turns it against them. By showing that similar narrations exist against Ali, he exposes the inconsistency in their argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully to grasp the overall argument.
2
Identify the reversal
Notice how Baqillani applies the same standard to Ali that the Shiites used for Uthman. The key is the parallelism.
3
Analyze the examples
Look at the specific cases of Talha, al-Zubayr, and A'isha. Compare them to the narrations about Abd al-Rahman.
Baqillani claims these are even stronger evidence against Ali.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن لم تقنع الشيعة وأبت إلا إبطال إمامة عثمان بهذا التأويل والروايات التي ليست بثابتة عن عبد الرحمن وإن كان قد عقدها في الأصل طوعاً واختياراً عن رأي ومشورة وإخبار الناس أنه وجد الصحابة لا يعدلون بعثمان أحداً عاد ذلك بأعظم الضرر عليهم ووجب عليهم به القدح في إمامة علي لأجل إنكار طلحة والزبير وعائشة لفعله وخلع طلحة والزبير له وإقراره بذلك على ما قد روي بمثل رواية ما ادعوه على عبد الرحمن في قوله في عثمان وقوله بالبصرة: بايعاني بالمدينة وخلعاني بالعراق، وقولهم في جواب ذلك: بايعناك على أن تقتل قتلة عثمان، وقول طلحة: بايعت واللج على قفي، وقول الزبير: بايعته أيدينا ولم تبايعه قلوبنا وقد كان أحضرا مكرهين فهما أعذر في خلعهما لعلي من عبد الرحمن في خلعه لعثمان ولأجل أن المطالبة بدم عثمان أمر ليس يقع التأويل في مثله وإن كان الحق في يد علي ومعه دون كل من خالفه وما نقم أحد على عثمان شيئاً فيه شبهة ولا متعلق وعلى أن عثمان لم يقعد عنه أحد دعاه إلى نصرته أيام حصاره وسعى أهل الفتنة عليه ; بل كانوا يبدلون أنفسهم ونصرتهم ويقولون: دعنا نكن أنصار الله مرتين! فيأبى ذلك ويمنعهم منه. وعلي عليه السلام قعد عن نصرته كثير ممن دعاه إلى القتال معه من جلة الصحابة كسعد وسعيد بن زيد بن عمرو بن نفيل
If the Shiites are not convinced and insist on invalidating Uthman's imamate based on this interpretation and the narrations that are not firmly established from Abd al-Rahman, even though he originally made the contract willingly and by choice based on opinion, consultation, and the people's informing him that he found the Companions consider none equal to Uthman, then that would return with greater harm upon them, and they would be obliged to impugn the imamate of Ali due to the disapproval of Talha and al-Zubayr and A'isha of his action, and the removal of Talha and al-Zubayr of him (Ali), and his acknowledgment of that, according to what has been narrated similar to the narration they claimed from Abd al-Rahman regarding his statement about Uthman and his statement in Basra: 'They gave me allegiance in Medina and they broke allegiance with me in Iraq', and their statement in response: 'We gave you allegiance on condition that you kill the killers of Uthman', and the statement of Talha: 'I gave allegiance while the sword was on my neck', and the statement of al-Zubayr: 'Our hands gave him allegiance but our hearts did not give him allegiance, and they were both brought under compulsion.' So they are more excusable in their removal of Ali than Abd al-Rahman in his removal of Uthman. And because demanding blood for Uthman is a matter about which interpretation does not occur (it is clear), even if the truth was with Ali and he held it, and everyone who opposed him was wrong. And no one criticized Uthman regarding anything that had ambiguity or any basis. And also, no one who was called to support Uthman during the siege held back from him; rather, the people of fitnah strove against him, but the others would offer themselves and their support and say: 'Let us be the helpers of Allah twice!' but he (Uthman) refused and prevented them. And Ali, peace be upon him, was not supported by many of those whom he called to fight with him from the great Companions, such as Sa'd and Sa'id ibn Zayd ibn Amr ibn Nufayl.
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage is a powerful rebuttal using the opponent's own method. Baqillani argues that if the Shiites accept weak narrations to invalidate Uthman's caliphate, then they must also accept similar narrations that would invalidate Ali's caliphate. He lists examples: Talha and al-Zubayr's revolt against Ali, their statements that they were coerced, etc. He then argues that the criticisms against Uthman are baseless, while the criticisms against Ali are more serious because they involve clear matters like demanding blood for Uthman. He also contrasts the support for Uthman during the siege with the lack of support for Ali from some prominent Companions. Thus, the Shiite position is self-contradictory.

Key Terms
إمامة (imamate)
خلع (removal)
بيعة (allegiance)
جلة الصحابة (great Companions)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That only Uthman's caliphate is questionable based on certain narrations.
Correction: Baqillani shows that applying the same standard would undermine Ali's caliphate.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, if the Shiites accept the narrations about Abd al-Rahman's regret, what would be the consequence for Ali's caliphate?
A) It would be strengthened
B) It would also be invalidated by similar narrations
C) It would remain unaffected
D) It would become subject to interpretation

Key Takeaway
Baqillani demonstrates that the Shiite argument against Uthman's caliphate is self-defeating because the same logic would invalidate Ali's imamate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read about the conflicts among the Companions, do you instinctively side with one group or another? What does this lesson teach you about the danger of using weak evidence to judge those whom Allah has praised? How can you apply this to your own judgments about Muslims today?
?
Have you ever used a flawed argument to criticize someone, only to find it could be used against you? How does Baqillani's reductio challenge you to be more consistent in your reasoning?
?
The Shiite position recoils on itself. Where in your own beliefs or actions is there a similar inconsistency that you need to address? What step will you take today to ensure your convictions are built on solid, balanced evidence?

The Parallel Argument Against Shi'a Critiques
Baqillani presents a parallel argument to refute Shi'a attacks on Uthman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses a parallel argument to show that Shi'a criticisms of Uthman's imamate would also undermine Ali's imamate.

Core Idea
Shi'a arguments against Uthman backfire on Ali.

Baqillani begins by pointing out that the very evidence the Shi'a use to attack Uthman's imamate—such as the role of Abd al-Rahman and depositions—applies even more strongly to Ali. He lists examples from Talha, al-Zubayr, and other Companions to show that if such evidence invalidates an imamate, then Ali's imamate would be even more vulnerable. This sets up a powerful tu quoque argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English carefully. Notice how Baqillani builds his parallel: if X counts against Uthman, then a similar Y counts against Ali.
2
Identify the parallel cases
Find where Baqillani compares the deposing of Uthman by Abd al-Rahman to the deposing of Ali by Talha and al-Zubayr. Note the additional details like duress and the demand for blood.
3
Consider the implications
Reflect on why Baqillani thinks the Shi'a cannot escape this parallel. What would happen if they accepted that these actions invalidate an imamate?
They would have to reject Ali's imamate, which they do not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التي ليست بثابتة عن عبد الرحمن وإن كان قد عقدها في الأصل طوعاً واختياراً عن رأي ومشورة وإخبار الناس أنه وجد الصحابة لا يعدلون بعثمان أحداً عاد ذلك بأعظم الضرر عليهم ووجب عليهم به القدح في إمامة علي لأجل إنكار طلحة والزبير وعائشة لفعله وخلع طلحة والزبير له وإقراره بذلك على ما قد روي بمثل رواية ما ادعوه على عبد الرحمن في قوله في عثمان وقوله بالبصرة: بايعاني بالمدينة وخلعاني بالعراق، وقولهم في جواب ذلك: بايعناك على أن تقتل قتلة عثمان، وقول طلحة: بايعت واللج على قفي [؟]. وقول الزبير: بايعته أيدينا ولم تبايعه قلوبنا وقد كان أحضرا مكرهين فهما أعذر في خلعهما لعلي من عبد الرحمن في خلعه لعثمان ولأجل أن المطالبة بدم عثمان أمر ليس يقع التأويل في مثله وإن كان الحق في يد علي ومعه دون كل من خالفه وما نقم أحد على عثمان شيئاً فيه شبهة ولا متعلق وعلى أن عثمان لم يقعد عنه أحد دعاه إلى نصرته أيام حصاره وسعى أهل الفتنة عليه؛ بل كانوا يبدلون أنفسهم ونصرتهم ويقولون: دعنا نكن أنصار الله مرتين! فيأبى ذلك ويمنعهم منه. وعلي عليه السلام قعد عن نصرته كثير ممن دعاه إلى القتال معه من جلة الصحابة كسعد وسعيد بن زيد بن عمرو بن نفيل وعبد الله بن عمر ومحمد بن مسلمة وأسامة بن زيد وسلامة بن وقش وغيرهم ممن لا يحصى كثرة فيجب أن يكون ذلك أظهر في القدح في إمامته وأجدر مما تعلق على عثمان. ونحن نبرأ إلى الله تعالى من القدح في إمامتهما جميعاً غير أن الشيعة تفتح على أنفسها من هذا الباب ما لا قبل لهم بدفعه. وليس تفسد إمامة علي بخلع من عقدها له ولا بالتأويل عليها بأنها عقدت على شرط فيها ولا يوهنها قعود من قعد عنها فكذلك لا تبطل إمامة عثمان بما حكوه عن عبد الرحمن ولا بسعي أوغاد وأهل فتنة إليه وتعديهم عليه لأن إمامته قد ثبتت وصحت فلا يقدح فيها شيء مما ذكروه. فإن قالت الشيعة: نحن لا نعتبر بقول طلحة والزبير وخلعهما وقعودهما لأن طريق الإمامة النص من النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قيل لهم: فليس يجب أن ينزلوا معنا إلى الكلام في إمامة عثمان وعقد عبد الرحمن وخلعه لأن الخوض فيها عندكم منكر فإن قالوا: إنما نسألكم ويلزمكم على مذهب أهل الاختيار، قيل لهم: قد أبنا لكم أن ذلك لا يلزم على أصولنا وأنه لو لزم لعاد بإبطال إمامة علي؛ وذلك فاسد.
Which are not established from Abd al-Rahman, even if he had originally made the pledge voluntarily and by choice, based on opinion and consultation, and informing people that he found the Companions not preferring anyone over Uthman, that would return with the greatest harm upon them, and it would be incumbent upon them to impugn the imamate of Ali because of the denial of Talha and al-Zubayr and Aisha of his action, and the deposing of Talha and al-Zubayr of him, and his acknowledgment of that according to what has been narrated similar to what they claimed against Abd al-Rahman regarding his statement about Uthman and his statement in Basra: 'They pledged allegiance to me in Medina and deposed me in Iraq,' and their response to that: 'We pledged allegiance to you on condition that you kill the murderers of Uthman,' and the statement of Talha: 'I pledged allegiance with the sword on my neck [؟],' and the statement of al-Zubayr: 'Our hands pledged allegiance to him but our hearts did not pledge allegiance,' and they had been brought under duress, so they are more excusable in their deposing of Ali than Abd al-Rahman in his deposing of Uthman, and because the demand for the blood of Uthman is a matter in which interpretation does not occur, even if the truth was with Ali and with him to the exclusion of all who opposed him. And no one found fault with Uthman for anything ambiguous or doubtful, and Uthman did not have anyone refuse him when he called them to his support during his siege, and the people of sedition sought against him; rather they were sacrificing themselves and their support and saying: 'Let us be the helpers of God twice!' but he refused that and prevented them from it. And Ali, peace be upon him, had many of those whom he called to fight with him among the eminent Companions refuse to support him, such as Sa'd, Sa'id ibn Zayd ibn Amr ibn Nufayl, Abdullah ibn Umar, Muhammad ibn Maslama, Usama ibn Zayd, Salama ibn Waqsh, and others beyond count. So that should be more apparent in impugning his imamate and more worthy than what they adduced against Uthman. And we seek refuge with God Almighty from impugning the imamate of both of them, but the Shi'a open against themselves a door they cannot repel. And the imamate of Ali is not invalidated by the deposing of those who pledged to him, nor by the interpretation that it was made conditional, nor is it weakened by the refusal of those who refused him. Likewise, the imamate of Uthman is not invalidated by what they narrated from Abd al-Rahman, nor by the scheming of vile people and people of sedition against him and their transgression, because his imamate has been established and confirmed, so nothing they mentioned detracts from it. If the Shi'a say: 'We do not consider the statement of Talha and al-Zubayr and their deposing and refusal, because the way of imamate is the text (nass) from the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace,' it is said to them: 'Then they should not descend with us into discussion about the imamate of Uthman and the pledge of Abd al-Rahman and his deposing, because engaging in that is objectionable according to you.' If they say: 'We only ask you and it is incumbent upon you according to the school of choice (ikhtiyar),' it is said to them: 'We have explained to you that this is not incumbent upon us according to our principles, and that if it were incumbent, it would lead to the invalidation of the imamate of Ali, and that is false.'
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Shi'a critique of Uthman's imamate. Baqillani uses a two-pronged argument. First, he shows that the same evidence the Shi'a use against Uthman (the role of Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf) would, if accepted, also impeach Ali's imamate, because Talha and al-Zubayr deposed Ali under circumstances that were even more excusable (they were coerced, and their objection was about the blood of Uthman, a matter not open to interpretation). Moreover, many respected Companions refused to support Ali, which would be even more damaging. So the Shi'a argument backfires. Second, Baqillani asserts that both imamates are valid and immune to such critiques: Ali's imamate is not invalidated by depositions or refusals, and similarly Uthman's imamate is not invalidated by the actions of Abd al-Rahman or the seditionists. The third part is an objection-and-answer: the Shi'a claim they rely on nass (divine appointment), not choice (ikhtiyar), so the parallel does not apply. Baqillani responds that if the Shi'a reject discussion based on choice, then they should not engage in this debate at all; if they choose to engage on those terms, their argument fails because it would also invalidate Ali's imamate. Thus the argument is consistent and the Shi'a position is self-defeating.

Key Terms
القدح في الإمامة
الإمامة
البيعة
الخلع
التأويل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Baqillani is actually criticizing Ali's imamate.
Correction: Baqillani explicitly says he seeks refuge from impugning either imamate; he is only using a hypothetical to refute the Shi'a.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, why would the Shi'a criticism of Uthman also apply to Ali?
A) Because Ali was also chosen by Abd al-Rahman.
B) Because Talha and al-Zubayr deposed Ali under circumstances similar to those alleged against Uthman.
C) Because Ali was not supported by the Prophet's companions.
D) Because Ali's imamate was based on nass, not ikhtiyar.

Key Takeaway
Shi'a criticisms of Uthman's imamate, if taken seriously, would also undermine Ali's imamate, exposing an inconsistency in their position.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time when you used someone else’s logic against them in a debate. Did you follow that logic to its conclusion even when it made you uncomfortable? What would it take for you to admit that your own reasoning could be turned against you, as Baqillani does here?
?
Baqillani refuses to impugn either Uthman or Ali, despite the historical controversies. Is there a person or group you’ve been quick to judge? What would it cost you to adopt Baqillani’s restraint and see the situation from a broader perspective?
?
The Shi'a argument relies on selective evidence—what fits their narrative. Where in your life are you picking and choosing evidence to support a conclusion you already hold, ignoring the full picture? Will you commit to seeking truth even if it undermines your preferred position?

The Nass Objection and Its Rebuttal
Baqillani answers the Shi'a nass objection and shows it is self-defeating.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes the Shi'a objection that they rely on nass (divine text) for imamate, not on ikhtiyar (choice), and why this does not save their critique of Uthman.

Core Idea
Shi'a reliance on nass does not rescue their argument; it only makes it irrelevant or self-defeating.

The Shi'a may try to escape the parallel by claiming that imamate is established by nass (divine appointment) and not by ikhtiyar (choice). Therefore, they argue, the actions of Companions like Talha and al-Zubayr are irrelevant. Baqillani responds by pointing out that if they truly hold to nass, they should not engage in a debate based on ikhtiyar at all. Alternatively, if they do engage on those terms, their argument fails because it would also invalidate Ali's imamate. This tight rebuttal closes the door on the Shi'a objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic and translation of the final section where the Shi'a objection is raised and Baqillani responds.
2
Analyze the two-part response
Baqillani gives two replies: either the Shi'a should not discuss Uthman's imamate at all (since they reject ikhtiyar), or if they do, their argument fails because it would invalidate Ali's imamate.
Notice how he forces them into a dilemma.
3
Understand the self-defeating nature
Reflect on why the Shi'a position is self-defeating: they cannot consistently argue against Uthman while holding to nass without undermining their own position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التي ليست بثابتة عن عبد الرحمن وإن كان قد عقدها في الأصل طوعاً واختياراً عن رأي ومشورة وإخبار الناس أنه وجد الصحابة لا يعدلون بعثمان أحداً عاد ذلك بأعظم الضرر عليهم ووجب عليهم به القدح في إمامة علي لأجل إنكار طلحة والزبير وعائشة لفعله وخلع طلحة والزبير له وإقراره بذلك على ما قد روي بمثل رواية ما ادعوه على عبد الرحمن في قوله في عثمان وقوله بالبصرة: بايعاني بالمدينة وخلعاني بالعراق، وقولهم في جواب ذلك: بايعناك على أن تقتل قتلة عثمان، وقول طلحة: بايعت واللج على قفي [؟]. وقول الزبير: بايعته أيدينا ولم تبايعه قلوبنا وقد كان أحضرا مكرهين فهما أعذر في خلعهما لعلي من عبد الرحمن في خلعه لعثمان ولأجل أن المطالبة بدم عثمان أمر ليس يقع التأويل في مثله وإن كان الحق في يد علي ومعه دون كل من خالفه وما نقم أحد على عثمان شيئاً فيه شبهة ولا متعلق وعلى أن عثمان لم يقعد عنه أحد دعاه إلى نصرته أيام حصاره وسعى أهل الفتنة عليه؛ بل كانوا يبدلون أنفسهم ونصرتهم ويقولون: دعنا نكن أنصار الله مرتين! فيأبى ذلك ويمنعهم منه. وعلي عليه السلام قعد عن نصرته كثير ممن دعاه إلى القتال معه من جلة الصحابة كسعد وسعيد بن زيد بن عمرو بن نفيل وعبد الله بن عمر ومحمد بن مسلمة وأسامة بن زيد وسلامة بن وقش وغيرهم ممن لا يحصى كثرة فيجب أن يكون ذلك أظهر في القدح في إمامته وأجدر مما تعلق على عثمان. ونحن نبرأ إلى الله تعالى من القدح في إمامتهما جميعاً غير أن الشيعة تفتح على أنفسها من هذا الباب ما لا قبل لهم بدفعه. وليس تفسد إمامة علي بخلع من عقدها له ولا بالتأويل عليها بأنها عقدت على شرط فيها ولا يوهنها قعود من قعد عنها فكذلك لا تبطل إمامة عثمان بما حكوه عن عبد الرحمن ولا بسعي أوغاد وأهل فتنة إليه وتعديهم عليه لأن إمامته قد ثبتت وصحت فلا يقدح فيها شيء مما ذكروه. فإن قالت الشيعة: نحن لا نعتبر بقول طلحة والزبير وخلعهما وقعودهما لأن طريق الإمامة النص من النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قيل لهم: فليس يجب أن ينزلوا معنا إلى الكلام في إمامة عثمان وعقد عبد الرحمن وخلعه لأن الخوض فيها عندكم منكر فإن قالوا: إنما نسألكم ويلزمكم على مذهب أهل الاختيار، قيل لهم: قد أبنا لكم أن ذلك لا يلزم على أصولنا وأنه لو لزم لعاد بإبطال إمامة علي؛ وذلك فاسد.
Which are not established from Abd al-Rahman, even if he had originally made the pledge voluntarily and by choice, based on opinion and consultation, and informing people that he found the Companions not preferring anyone over Uthman, that would return with the greatest harm upon them, and it would be incumbent upon them to impugn the imamate of Ali because of the denial of Talha and al-Zubayr and Aisha of his action, and the deposing of Talha and al-Zubayr of him, and his acknowledgment of that according to what has been narrated similar to what they claimed against Abd al-Rahman regarding his statement about Uthman and his statement in Basra: 'They pledged allegiance to me in Medina and deposed me in Iraq,' and their response to that: 'We pledged allegiance to you on condition that you kill the murderers of Uthman,' and the statement of Talha: 'I pledged allegiance with the sword on my neck [؟],' and the statement of al-Zubayr: 'Our hands pledged allegiance to him but our hearts did not pledge allegiance,' and they had been brought under duress, so they are more excusable in their deposing of Ali than Abd al-Rahman in his deposing of Uthman, and because the demand for the blood of Uthman is a matter in which interpretation does not occur, even if the truth was with Ali and with him to the exclusion of all who opposed him. And no one found fault with Uthman for anything ambiguous or doubtful, and Uthman did not have anyone refuse him when he called them to his support during his siege, and the people of sedition sought against him; rather they were sacrificing themselves and their support and saying: 'Let us be the helpers of God twice!' but he refused that and prevented them from it. And Ali, peace be upon him, had many of those whom he called to fight with him among the eminent Companions refuse to support him, such as Sa'd, Sa'id ibn Zayd ibn Amr ibn Nufayl, Abdullah ibn Umar, Muhammad ibn Maslama, Usama ibn Zayd, Salama ibn Waqsh, and others beyond count. So that should be more apparent in impugning his imamate and more worthy than what they adduced against Uthman. And we seek refuge with God Almighty from impugning the imamate of both of them, but the Shi'a open against themselves a door they cannot repel. And the imamate of Ali is not invalidated by the deposing of those who pledged to him, nor by the interpretation that it was made conditional, nor is it weakened by the refusal of those who refused him. Likewise, the imamate of Uthman is not invalidated by what they narrated from Abd al-Rahman, nor by the scheming of vile people and people of sedition against him and their transgression, because his imamate has been established and confirmed, so nothing they mentioned detracts from it. If the Shi'a say: 'We do not consider the statement of Talha and al-Zubayr and their deposing and refusal, because the way of imamate is the text (nass) from the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace,' it is said to them: 'Then they should not descend with us into discussion about the imamate of Uthman and the pledge of Abd al-Rahman and his deposing, because engaging in that is objectionable according to you.' If they say: 'We only ask you and it is incumbent upon you according to the school of choice (ikhtiyar),' it is said to them: 'We have explained to you that this is not incumbent upon us according to our principles, and that if it were incumbent, it would lead to the invalidation of the imamate of Ali, and that is false.'
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Shi'a critique of Uthman's imamate. Baqillani uses a two-pronged argument. First, he shows that the same evidence the Shi'a use against Uthman (the role of Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf) would, if accepted, also impeach Ali's imamate, because Talha and al-Zubayr deposed Ali under circumstances that were even more excusable (they were coerced, and their objection was about the blood of Uthman, a matter not open to interpretation). Moreover, many respected Companions refused to support Ali, which would be even more damaging. So the Shi'a argument backfires. Second, Baqillani asserts that both imamates are valid and immune to such critiques: Ali's imamate is not invalidated by depositions or refusals, and similarly Uthman's imamate is not invalidated by the actions of Abd al-Rahman or the seditionists. The third part is an objection-and-answer: the Shi'a claim they rely on nass (divine appointment), not choice (ikhtiyar), so the parallel does not apply. Baqillani responds that if the Shi'a reject discussion based on choice, then they should not engage in this debate at all; if they choose to engage on those terms, their argument fails because it would also invalidate Ali's imamate. Thus the argument is consistent and the Shi'a position is self-defeating.

Key Terms
النص
الاختيار
الإمامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the Shi'a nass objection is a valid escape from Baqillani's parallel.
Correction: Baqillani shows that the nass objection either prevents the Shi'a from arguing about Uthman at all or, if they argue, their own reasoning turns against them.

Checkpoint
What is Baqillani's first response to the Shi'a claim that imamate is based on nass?
A) He accepts that nass is the only valid basis.
B) He says they should not discuss Uthman's imamate because it is based on ikhtiyar.
C) He argues that nass also supports Uthman.
D) He ignores the objection.

Key Takeaway
The Shi'a appeal to nass does not rescue their critique; it either silences their argument or turns it against their own position.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever clung to a principle to avoid addressing a difficult issue, only to realize that same principle undermines your own position? How did you respond, and what does that reveal about your commitment to truth over convenience?
?
This passage shows that Baqillani held the Shi'a to the logical consequences of their own claims. Reflect on an area of your life where you might be inconsistent—applying one standard to yourself and another to others. What would it cost you to be truly consistent?
?
Baqillani’s rebuttal is not just intellectual; it forces the opponent to either be silent or accept a falsehood. When you argue for your beliefs, do you aim to force the other person into a corner with logic, or do you seek to guide them toward truth with compassion and patience? Which approach is more faithful to the spirit of this lesson?
