البقية قوم من بني عبد الدار فقتل منهم سوى عثمان أربعة نفر وقتل العبد الأسود وارتُتْ مروان بن الحكم خارج الدار وأُنْخِنَ الحسن حتى حُمِل مغلوباً بألم الجراح. ولما رأت نائلة بنت الفرافصة زوج عثمان وقع السيف برزت وألقت نفسها عليه فأصابتها ضربة اندرتْ من يدها ثلاث أصابع، وضرب بعض أولئك الفجرة يده عليها وقال: «ما أكبر عجيزتها، نقلونيها» وصاح الآخرون ألحقوا بيت المال وأغاروا بديئاً على رَحْلِ عثمان وما كان في داره ثم تناولوا ما أمكنهم أخذه من بيت المال وأضرموا الدار عليه بالنار فاحترق أكثر أبوابها. وذُكر أن عمرو بن الحَمِقِ قال : «طعنتُ طعنات منها ثلاث لله وست لغير الله». وقد علم كلُّ مسلم أنصف نفسه أن ما فعله القوم به ليس من الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر في شيء وأنه أبعد الأمور عن الحق وعن مصلحة الأمة وأدعاها إلى تفريق الكلمة وشتات الرأي وتوهين الدين والإذلال لسلطان المسلمين والتَّوَثْب على أئمتهم وتوخّي إضعاف أمرهم وقصر هممهم وأيديهم عن إقامة الدين وتنفيذ أحكام المسلمين وأن عثمان رضي الله عنه لو كان في الحقيقة قد ارتد عن دينه أو زنى بعد إحصانه لم يستحق سفك دمه على ذلك الوجه وإحراقهم داره ونهب تراثه والمطالبة بتنفيل زوجته وهذا أظهر وأبين من أن نحتاج فيه إلى إقامة الدليل على ظلم فاعله وتعديه. وعلى أن ذلك أجمع لو وجب عليه وكان من حدود الله تعالى في شريعة لم يكن لهؤلاء القوم توليه وإقامته وإنما ذلك إلى سلطان المسلمين ولا أقل من أن يكون للأماثل منهم أهل الحل والعقد ومن يُقَدَّرُ فيه الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر دون من ذكرناه. وكل من ادعي عليه قتله من الصحابة فقد كُذِبَ عليه وأضيف إليه ما ليس منه بسبيل كعلي وطلحة والزبير رضوان الله عليهم وما من هؤلاء أجمع أحد إلا وقد أظهر المطالبة بدمه ولعن قتلته وأظهر البراءة منهم والتأسف على ألا يمكنه إقامة الحق عليهم. وهذا ظاهر معلوم من حال عليّ وطَلْحَةَ والزبير وما وراء ذلك إنما هو من الشواذ وأخبار الآحاد ولا يحل لمسلم اتقى الله وعرف قدر الصحابة أن يضيف إلى أحد منهم قتل عثمان والرضا به والخذلان مع دعائه إلى نُصرَتِه والدفع عنه بأخبارِ آحاد يعارضها مثلها تارة وما هو أقوى منها أخرى ويكون الظاهر من قول عليّ وطلحة والزبير بخلافها وفي نقيضها لأن الظاهر المعلوم لا يُتْرَكُ لروايات غير معلومة بل لو لم يظهر منهم مثل هذا لكانت مثل هذه الأخبار مدفوعة بما ورد من أمثالها في نقيضها ومعارضتها وكيف يجوز لذي علم ودين أن يضيف إلى أدونِ الصحابة بعض ما يوجب الفسق من قتل عثمان أو التأليب عليه أو خذلانه بروايات لا تساوي مدادها ولا الاشتغال بالإصغاء إليها وقد ظهر عُدْوَان من ذكرناه عليه وتوليه لقتله وفي ذلك يقول الشاعر: ألا إن خير الناس بعد ثلاثة قَتِيلُ التجيبي الذي جاء من مصر وذكر أيضاً محمد بن أبي بكر وغيره في أشعار كثيرة مشهورة، وقد ذكرناها في غير هذا الكتاب.
And he turned away and mentioned that he did not touch him in some narrations, so al-Ghafiqi and Kinana knew that he turned away out of shyness, so they rushed against him, and al-Tajibi struck him with a blow that threw him on his side with the mushaf in his lap. When blood fell on it, he closed it, then pushed it aside, and others struck him. The remaining group fought from Banu Abd al-Dar, and four of them were killed besides Uthman, and the black slave was killed, and Marwan ibn al-Hakam was wounded outside the house, and al-Hasan was injured until he was carried overwhelmed by the pain of the wounds. When Na'ila bint al-Furafisa, the wife of Uthman, saw the sword, she came out and threw herself upon him, and a blow struck her, cutting off three of her fingers. Some of those wicked ones struck his hand saying: 'How large is her posterior! Extricate her for us!' And others called out: 'Go to the treasury!' and they initially plundered Uthman's belongings and what was in his house, then they took what they could from the treasury, and set fire to his house, and most of its doors were burned. It was mentioned that Amr ibn al-Hamiq said: 'I stabbed him with stabs: three for God and six for other than God.' And every Muslim who is fair to himself knows that what these people did to him is in no way part of enjoining good and forbidding evil, and it is the farthest thing from truth and from the welfare of the umma, and the most conducive to division of the word, dispersion of opinion, weakening of religion, humiliation of the authority of the Muslims, aggression against their imams, seeking to weaken their command, and curtailing their ambitions and hands from establishing religion and executing the judgments of the Muslims. And if Uthman, may God be pleased with him, had actually apostatized from his religion or committed adultery after being married, he would not have deserved to have his blood shed in that manner, nor their burning his house, plundering his inheritance, and demanding his wife. This is more apparent and clearer than that we need to establish proof of the injustice and transgression of its doer. And even if all that had been incumbent upon him and had been among the limits of God in the Sharia, it was not for these people to undertake it and execute it; rather that is for the authority of the Muslims, at the very least for the notable ones among them, the people of binding and loosening, and those who are considered for enjoining good and forbidding evil, not for those we mentioned. And whoever among the Companions is accused of killing him has been slandered, and something that is not from him has been attributed to him, like Ali, Talha, and al-Zubayr, may God be pleased with them. There is not one among all of them who did not manifest demanding vengeance for his blood, cursing his killers, manifesting disassociation from them, and regretting that he could not establish the truth against them. This is apparent and known from the condition of Ali, Talha, and al-Zubayr. What is beyond that is only from the anomalous reports and isolated reports. It is not permissible for a Muslim who fears God and knows the standing of the Companions to attribute to any of them the killing of Uthman, or being pleased with it, or abandoning him despite his call for help and defense, based on isolated reports that are contradicted by similar reports sometimes, and by stronger reports other times, and the apparent statements of Ali, Talha, and al-Zubayr are contrary to them and in opposition to them, because the apparent known is not abandoned for unknown narrations. Even if such statements had not appeared from them, such reports would be rejected due to the opposite reports that contradict them. How can a person of knowledge and religion attribute to the least of the Companions something that necessitates sinfulness, such as killing Uthman or inciting against him or abandoning him, based on reports that are not worth their ink nor the effort of listening to them, when the transgression of those we mentioned against him and their undertaking his killing is apparent? And about that, the poet said: 'Indeed, the best of people after three is the one killed by al-Tajibi who came from Egypt.' And Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr and others are also mentioned in many famous poems, and we have mentioned them in other than this book.
Source pages p. 530

Commentary
This passage is a historical and theological defense of the Companions, especially Ali, Talha, and Zubayr, against accusations of involvement in the murder of Caliph Uthman. The author begins by narrating the attack on Uthman in detail: how al-Tajibi struck him, how blood fell on the mushaf, and how Na'ila was wounded defending him. He then refutes any justification for the attackers' actions, arguing that even if Uthman had committed a sin such as apostasy or adultery, the punishment would not have been mob lynching, and the attackers were not authorized to carry out divine limits. Such authority belongs to the Muslim ruler and the people of binding and loosening (ahl al-hall wa al-'aqd). He then addresses accusations against the Companions: anyone claiming that Ali, Talha, or Zubayr participated in the killing is lying, because their known stance was to demand justice, curse the killers, and dissociate from them. The author dismisses any contrary reports as anomalous (shawadh) and isolated (akhbar ahad), which are outweighed by the well-known facts and stronger reports. He concludes that it is impermissible for a Muslim who fears God and respects the Companions to attribute such evil to them based on weak reports, especially when the transgression of the actual perpetrators is evident. The passage ends with a poetic verse and a reference to more details in another book.

Key Terms
الصحابة
أخبار الآحاد
الظاهر المعلوم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that any historical report about the Companions is equally valid.
Correction: Al-Baqillani teaches that the well-established conduct of the Companions takes precedence over isolated reports that contradict it.

Checkpoint
According to al-Baqillani, what was the known stance of Ali, Talha, and al-Zubayr regarding Uthman's murder?
A) They supported the attackers
B) They remained silent
C) They demanded vengeance and cursed the killers
D) They fled Medina

Key Takeaway
The Companions are exonerated from involvement in Uthman's murder, and isolated reports cannot override their well-known righteousness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever believed a negative story about someone based on a single report without checking their known character? After reading this lesson, how will you change your approach to evaluating accusations?
?
The Companions' apparent stance was clear and aligned with their inner convictions. Is your own public stance aligned with your inner beliefs, or are you vulnerable to being misrepresented? What steps can you take to ensure your known actions reflect your true character?
?
This passage warns against attributing sin to others based on weak reports. Are there any people you have unjustly judged? How can you seek forgiveness and correct your view of them?

Defending the Companions from Accusations of Uthman's Killing
Baqillani refutes accusations against Companions for Uthman's killing using known apparent actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the principle of al-zaahir al-ma'loom (the apparent known) to reject isolated reports (akhbaar al-aahaad) that accuse the Companions of involvement in Uthman's killing.

Core Idea
The known character of the Companions outweighs weak isolated reports.

This passage from Imam al-Baqillani addresses a sensitive historical accusation: that some Companions were involved in the killing of Caliph Uthman. Baqillani does not rely on emotional appeals but on a methodological principle: what is openly known (al-zaahir al-ma'loom) from the Companions' actions cannot be overturned by isolated narrations (akhbaar al-aahaad). In this lesson, we will explore how he applies this principle to defend the honour of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then read the translation. Notice Baqillani's argument flow from general principle to specific defense.
2
Identify the key claim being refuted
Baqillani is responding to the accusation that some Companions, especially Ali, Talha, and al-Zubayr, were involved in Uthman's killing. Find where he states this claim.
The accusation is that they either killed him, approved of his death, or failed to support him when called.
3
Note the evidence for the Companions' innocence
How does Baqillani prove that Ali, Talha, and al-Zubayr were not involved? Look for their actions: demanding blood, cursing killers, disavowing them, and regretting inability to bring justice.
This is the 'apparent known' (al-zaahir al-ma'loom) from their states.
4
Understand the methodological rule
Baqillani classifies contrary reports as anomalous (shadhdh) and isolated (akhbar al-ahad). He argues that such reports cannot overturn the known apparent, especially when contradicted by stronger or similar reports.
This is a key principle in hadith criticism and kalam: the known apparent outweighs the obscure.
5
Reflect on the rhetorical conclusion
Notice Baqillani's rhetorical question and the poetic citation. How does he emphasize the weakness of the accusing reports?
He says the ink of those reports is not worth the effort to listen to them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أظهر وأبين من أن نحتاج فيه إلى إقامة الدليل على ظلم فاعله وتعديه . وعلى أن ذلك أجمع لو وجب عليه وكان من حدود الله تعالى في شريعة لم يكن لهؤلاء القوم توليه وإقامته وإنما ذلك إلى سلطان المسلمين ولا أقل من أن يكون للأماثل منهم أهل الحل والعقد ومن يُقَدَّرُ فيه الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر دون من ذكرناه . وكل من ادعي عليه قتله من الصحابة فقد كُذِبَ عليه وأضيف إليه ما ليس منه بسبيل كعلي وطلحة والزبير رضوان الله عليهم وما من هؤلاء أجمع أحد إلا وقد أظهر المطالبة بدمه ولعن قتلته وأظهر البراءة منهم والتأسف على ألا يمكنه إقامة الحق عليهم . وهذا ظاهر معلوم من حال عليّ وطَلْحَةَ والزبير وما وراء ذلك إنما هو من الشواذ وأخبار الآحاد ولا يحل لمسلم اتقى الله وعرف قدر الصحابة أن يضيف إلى أحد منهم قتل عثمان والرضا به والخذلان مع دعائه إلى نُصرَتِه والدفع عنه بأخبارِ آحاد يعارضها مثلها تارة ومـا هـو أقوى منها أخرى ويكون الظاهر من قول عليّ وطلحة والزبير بخلافها وفي نقيضها لأن الظاهر المعلوم لا يُتْرَكُ لروايات غير معلومة بل لو لم يظهر منهم مثل هذا لكانت مثل هذه الأخبار مدفوعة بما ورد من أمثالها في نقيضها ومعارضتها وكيف يجوز لذي علم ودين أن يضيف إلى أدونِ الصحابة بعض ما يوجب الفسق من قتل عثمان أو التأليب عليه أو خذلانه بروايات لا تساوي مدادها ولا الاشتغال بالإصغاء إليها وقد ظهر عُدْوَان من ذكرناه عليه وتوليه لقتله وفي ذلك يقول الشاعر: ألا إن خير الناس بعد ثلاثة قَتِيلُ التجيبي الذي جاء من مصر وذكر أيضاً محمد بن أبي بكر وغيره في أشعار كثيرة مشهورة، وقد ذكرناها في غير هذا الكتاب.
It is more apparent and clearer than that we need to establish proof of the injustice of its doer and his transgression. And that all of that, if it were obligatory upon him and were among the limits of God Almighty in the Sharia, would not be for these people to undertake and execute; rather, that is for the ruler of the Muslims, or at least for the most prominent among them, the people of binding and loosing, and whoever is deemed capable of commanding good and forbidding evil, not those we have mentioned. And every one of the Companions who has been accused of killing him has been lied about, and something that is not from him has been attributed to him, such as Ali, Talha, and al-Zubayr, may God be pleased with them. There is none among all these except that he has openly demanded his blood, cursed his killers, declared his disavowal of them, and regretted that he could not establish the truth against them. This is apparent and known from the state of Ali, Talha, and al-Zubayr. Whatever is beyond that is only from anomalous reports and isolated reports (akhbar al-ahad). It is not permissible for a Muslim who fears God and knows the status of the Companions to attribute to any of them the killing of Uthman, or satisfaction with it, or abandonment despite his call for help and defense, based on isolated reports that are contradicted by similar reports sometimes and by stronger ones other times, while the apparent from the statements of Ali, Talha, and al-Zubayr is contrary to them and in opposition to them. This is because the apparent known is not abandoned for unknown narrations. Even if such had not appeared from them, such reports would be repelled by reports similar to them in opposition and contradiction. How can a person of knowledge and religion attribute to the least of the Companions something that necessitates sin, such as killing Uthman or inciting against him or abandoning him, based on reports whose ink is not equal (in value) nor is it worth the effort to listen to them, while the enmity of those we have mentioned towards him and their undertaking of his killing has become apparent? And in that regard the poet says: 'Indeed, the best of people after three is the slain of al-Tujaybi who came from Egypt.' And Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr and others are also mentioned in many famous poems, which we have mentioned in another book.
Source pages p. 531

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that some Companions, specifically Ali, Talha, and al-Zubayr, were involved in the killing of Caliph Uthman or approved of it. Baqillani begins by stating that the injustice of the killers is too obvious to require proof. He then argues that even if punishing the killers were obligatory, it would be the duty of the Muslim ruler or the elite scholars (ahl al-hall wa al-'aqd), not just anyone. Then he shifts to defending the Companions: every Companion accused of killing Uthman has been falsely accused. He emphasizes that Ali, Talha, and al-Zubayr all publicly demanded Uthman's blood, cursed his killers, and expressed regret that they could not bring justice. This is well-known from their actions. Any reports claiming otherwise are anomalous (shadhdh) and isolated (akhbar al-ahad). He then states that it is impermissible for a Muslim who fears God and knows the noble status of the Companions to attribute to any of them the killing of Uthman, satisfaction with it, or failure to support him, based on weak isolated reports that are contradicted by similar or stronger reports. The apparent actions and statements of these Companions contradict such reports, and the known apparent cannot be abandoned for unknown narrations. Even if they had not shown the opposite, such reports would be rejected due to contradictory reports. He rhetorically asks how a person of knowledge and religion could attribute major sin to even the least of the Companions based on worthless narrations, when the enmity of the actual killers is clear. He then cites a poet's verse and mentions that he has discussed these poems elsewhere.

Key Terms
أخبار الآحاد
الظاهر المعلوم
الشواذ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some Companions, especially Ali, Talha, and al-Zubayr, were involved in or approved of Uthman's killing.
Correction: Baqillani demonstrates that these Companions publicly demanded Uthman's blood, cursed his killers, and expressed regret that they could not bring justice.

Checkpoint
What does Baqillani say about the reports that accuse Companions like Ali, Talha, and al-Zubayr of involvement in Uthman's killing?
A) They are widely accepted and must be followed.
B) They are anomalous isolated reports that contradict the known apparent actions of these Companions.
C) They prove that these Companions were sinful.
D) They are from multiple chains and thus authentic.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani defends the Companions by arguing that their well-known actions of demanding justice for Uthman cannot be overturned by weak isolated reports.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How often do you form a negative opinion about a fellow Muslim based on a single report or rumor you heard, while ignoring the many good deeds and upright character you have seen from them? What would it take for you to abandon that habit and seek the 'apparent known' about them?
?
Is there a respected scholar, leader, or companion of knowledge in your life against whom you hold a secret suspicion based on something you once heard? Will you now commit to verifying their well-known actions before allowing that suspicion to grow?
?
If you knew that a weak, isolated report about a person could never outweigh their clear good character, would you still pass on that report to others? What does your answer reveal about your own fear of Allah and respect for the honor of Muslims?

Baqillani's Refutation of Uthman's Alleged Letter
Baqillani evaluates a report about Uthman's letter to Ali during the siege.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's method of evaluating historical reports by examining internal contradictions and the apparent (zahir) state of affairs.

Core Idea
Historical reports are tested by consistency with known facts and authoritative statements.

Baqillani now turns to a specific historical report that has been used to cast doubt on Ali's role during the siege of Uthman. He shows that the report is not only isolated in transmission but also contradicts what is well-known about Uthman's own orders. By examining the report critically, he demonstrates how Sunni scholars assess historical narratives—not just on chain but on content.

Guided Path
1
Read the report and its context
Identify what the report says (Uthman wrote to Ali a desperate plea) and why it is problematic in the context of the siege.
The report is categorized as isolated (khabar al-ahad).
2
Examine Baqillani's internal evidence
Note how Baqillani points out contradictions: Ali sent al-Hasan to support Uthman, but Uthman turned him away; Uthman ordered everyone to sheathe swords and stay home; he freed slaves who complied.
These well-known actions contradict the report's claim.
3
Consider the alternative interpretation
Even if the report were true, Baqillani suggests Uthman's words could be an expression of distress, not an accusation of Ali.
This shows care for the Companion's reputation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما رُوِيَ عن عثمان أنه كتب إلى عليّ أيام الحصار: فإن كُنْتُ مأكولاً فكن خير آكــل وإلا فادركني ولما أمزق إنما هو أيضاً من روايات الآحاد وكيف يصح ذلك، وقد أنفذ علي الحَسَن لنصرته وعثمان يرده ويرد الناس عن الدفع عنه بالقتال لهم ويحملهم الرسائل إليهم بالوعظ لهم؟ وهذا معلوم ظاهر من حاله؛ وأنه قال: «من كان يظن أن لي في عنقه طاعة فليغمد سيفه وليلزم بيت»؛ وقال لعبيده: غمد منكم سيفه فهو حر لـوجـه الله»، ففعلوا إلا الأسود الذي قتل في الدار وهذا لا يشبه ما رووه من استنهاضه لعليّ ولأن في ذلك أيضاً قرفاً لعثمان في اتهامه لمثل عليّ رضوان الله عليه في هذا الباب. فكل ما جرى هذه مجری الروايات فإنه مردود والظاهر من عليّ تكذيب هذه الرواية من قوله: «والله ما قتلتُ عثمان ولا مالات على قتله». ويمكن لو صحت هذه الرواية أن يكون هذا القول من عثمان ليس على سبيل التهمة لعلي عليه السلام بل على طريق الاستزادة في وعظ القوم وكفهم وإرساله في هذا الباب وقد يقول الإنسان مثل هذا الكلام إذا حَزَبَه الأمر وفجئه مـا يخافه على غير سبيل الظنة والتهمة.
And what has been narrated from Uthman that he wrote to Ali during the siege: 'If I am to be eaten, then be the best eater, otherwise save me before I am torn apart' — this too is only from isolated reports (akhbar al-ahad). How can it be authentic, given that Ali sent al-Hasan to support him, while Uthman was turning him away and turning people away from fighting them, and sending messages to them with admonition? This is known and apparent from his state. And he said: 'Whoever thinks that I have any obedience due from him, let him sheathe his sword and stay in his house.' And he said to his slaves: 'Whoever of you sheathes his sword is free for the sake of God.' So they did so, except al-Aswad who was killed in the house. This does not resemble what they narrated about him urging Ali (to come). Moreover, in that there is a blemish on Uthman for accusing someone like Ali, may God be pleased with him, in this matter. So every report that follows this course is rejected, and the apparent from Ali is the denial of this narration in his statement: 'By God, I did not kill Uthman nor did I aid in his killing.' And if this report were authentic, it could be that this statement from Uthman was not by way of suspicion of Ali, peace be upon him, but rather by way of seeking more in admonishing the people and restraining them, and sending him in this matter. A person may say such words when a matter distresses him and he is suddenly confronted with something he fears, without suspicion or accusation.
Source pages p. 532

Commentary
This passage is an evaluation and refutation of a specific report: that during the siege of his house, Uthman wrote to Ali saying, 'If I am to be eaten, then be the best eater, otherwise save me before I am torn apart.' Baqillani first categorizes this as an isolated report (khabar al-ahad). He then questions its authenticity by pointing out known facts: Ali had sent his son al-Hasan to support Uthman, but Uthman himself turned Ali and others away, instructing them not to fight. Uthman explicitly told people to sheathe their swords and stay home, and even freed his slaves who complied, except one who was killed. This contradicts the notion that Uthman was calling for help. Therefore, the report is rejected. Additionally, Baqillani notes that attributing such a request to Uthman would imply that Uthman suspected Ali, which is unbecoming. The apparent position of Ali, as known from his own statement, is that he neither killed Uthman nor aided in his killing. Finally, Baqillani offers a possible interpretation if the report were considered authentic: Uthman's words might not have been an accusation but rather an expression of distress, seeking further admonition, a common human reaction in dire circumstances.

Key Terms
أخبار الآحاد
الظاهر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The report that Uthman wrote to Ali shows that Ali was hesitant to help or even complicit in Uthman's death.
Correction: Baqillani demonstrates that the report contradicts Uthman's own known orders to avoid fighting, and that Ali's actions and statements (sending al-Hasan, denying involvement) support his innocence.

Checkpoint
Why does Baqillani reject the report that Uthman wrote to Ali pleading for help during the siege?
A) Because the report is from multiple chains and contradicts itself.
B) Because the report is isolated and contradicts Uthman's known orders for everyone to stay home and not fight.
C) Because Ali himself denied receiving any letter.
D) Because the report is fabricated by the killers of Uthman.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani demonstrates that historical reports must be evaluated not only by their chain but also by their consistency with established facts and authoritative statements.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a negative story about a righteous person, do you test it against their established character, or does it affect your view? Baqillani examined the report against Uthman's known actions. What report about a fellow Muslim have you accepted without checking? Will you now commit to verifying such reports before forming an opinion?
?
Baqillani offered a charitable interpretation of Uthman's alleged words, even if the report were true. Have you ever misjudged someone's words because you assumed a bad intention? How can you apply the principle of seeking the best interpretation to your interactions starting today?
?
This lesson shows that great scholars defended the honor of the Companions. Do you have any lingering doubt about the integrity of any Sahabi? If so, what specific doubt? How will you actively seek to remove that doubt by learning more about their virtue as demonstrated by scholars like Baqillani?

Why the Companions Did Not Defend Uthman: Obedience to His Orders
Baqillani answers the objection about Companions' non-defence of Uthman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rationale behind the Companions' non-participation in defending Uthman, as explained by Baqillani, and how obedience to Uthman's own command constitutes a valid excuse.

Core Idea
The Companions obeyed Uthman's command, not abandoned him.

This lesson addresses a historical and theological objection: if Uthman was unjustly treated, why did the Companions not rush to his defence? Baqillani provides a clear answer rooted in the Companions' obedience to Uthman's explicit and repeated orders. Understanding this helps reconcile their apparent inaction with their piety and loyalty.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Start by reading the objection posed by the questioner: why didn't the Companions hasten to denounce the injustice and stop the rebels?
The objection assumes that visible injustice demands immediate action.
2
Understand the answer's structure
Notice how Baqillani begins with a strong denial ('God forbid'), then gives the reason: Uthman himself ordered the Companions to stay home and not confront the rebels.
The answer emphasizes that the Companions were not negligent; they followed the caliph's instructions.
3
Examine the supporting evidence
Pay attention to the example of Zayd ibn Thabit. Even when he came carrying his weapon, Uthman sent him away, reinforcing the order.
This shows that the command was explicit and repeatedly emphasized.
4
Reflect on the theological implication
Consider how this answer defends the Companions' honour and demonstrates their obedience to the caliph, while also preserving the principle of 'commanding good and forbidding evil'.
The Companions did not abandon Uthman; they obeyed him.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل : فإذا كان الأمر في هذا على ما وصفتم من ظلم القوم له وتعديهم عليه فما بال الصحابة لم يسارعوا إلى إنكار ذلك وصدهم عنه؟ وأي عذر لهم في إسلامه والتساهل في خذلانه؟ قيل له : معاذ الله أن يكون فيهم خذله أو قعد عن نصرته عند دعائه لهم وإنما لزموا بيوتهم لأنه أمرهم بذلك وكرره عليهم وناشدهم الله عزّ وجلّ وعرفهم أن الجيوش توافيه وأنه لا يرى منابذة الصحابة لأهل الفتنة وإنما يجب أن يُدْفَعُوا بأمثالهم ووكد هذا القول وضيقه على القوم وقد جاء زيد بن ثابت شاكاً في سلاحه وقال له :
If someone says: Since the matter is as you have described — the injustice of the people against him and their transgression against him — why did the Companions not hasten to denounce that and stop them? And what excuse do they have for abandoning him and being lenient in failing to support him? He is told: God forbid that there should be among them abandonment of him or sitting back from supporting him when he called them. Rather, they stayed in their houses because he ordered them to do so and repeated it to them, and he adjured them by God Almighty, and informed them that armies were coming to him, and that he did not see that the Companions should confront the people of sedition; rather, they should be repelled by their likes. He emphasized this statement and made it difficult for them. And Zayd ibn Thabit came carrying his weapon, and he said to him: ...
Source pages p. 532

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer. The objector asks: given the obvious injustice against Uthman, why didn't the Companions immediately denounce it and prevent it? What excuse can they have for abandoning him and being lax in supporting him? The answer begins with a strong denial: 'God forbid' that any Companion abandoned or failed to support him when called. The reason they stayed home is because Uthman himself commanded them to do so, repeatedly. He adjured them by God, told them that armies were coming to his aid, and expressed that he did not want the Companions to fight the rebels, as the rebels should be dealt with by their own kind. Uthman emphasized and insisted on this. The answer then gives an example: Zayd ibn Thabit came armed, and Uthman said to him... (the text cuts off). Thus, the Companions obeyed Uthman's explicit order, which absolves them of any blame.

Key Terms
الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر
أهل الفتنة
نصرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Companions failed to defend Uthman out of cowardice or apathy.
Correction: The Companions were obeying Uthman's own command to stay home and not confront the rebels.

Checkpoint
What reason does Baqillani give for the Companions not physically defending Uthman during the siege?
A) They were afraid of the rebels.
B) They did not consider it their duty.
C) Uthman himself ordered them to stay home and not fight.
D) They were not present in Medina at the time.

Key Takeaway
The Companions' inaction in defending Uthman was not abandonment but compliance with his explicit command.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

How does Uthman's unwavering command to his Companions challenge your instinct to override authority? Will you commit to trusting legitimate leadership more, even when it costs you the desire to act?
?
If you were one of the Companions outside Uthman's house, hearing him order you to stay back while he faced danger, what would have been harder: to obey and feel passive, or to disobey and fight? What does your answer reveal about your attachment to honor over obedience?
?
The objectors in this passage judged the Companions without knowing Uthman's order. Where in your life have you judged someone's inaction without understanding their reasons? Are you willing to suspend those judgments now and assume obedience to a higher command?

Refutation of the Report about Uthman's Letter to Ali
Baqillani refutes the report that Uthman wrote to Ali during the siege.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes a weak historical report by using transmission criticism and contextual consistency.

Core Idea
Weak reports contradict known historical facts.

In this passage, Baqillani takes on a controversial report from the siege of Uthman. He demonstrates the methodology of Kalam scholars in assessing historical narrations, using both transmission criticism and contextual consistency. This lesson will walk through his refutation and the principles it illustrates.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the English translation. Note the report Baqillani is refuting.
The report includes a poetic line: 'If I am eaten, then be the best eater...'
2
Identify the classification
Notice that Baqillani immediately labels the report as being from 'individual narrations' (riwayat al-ahad), which is a key point in his argument.
In Islamic scholarship, khabar ahad does not provide certainty.
3
Examine the evidence
List the pieces of evidence Baqillani presents against the report: Uthman's orders to stay home, his freeing of those who sheathed swords, and Ali's sending of al-Hasan.
These facts are presented as well-known and contradict the report.
4
Consider the alternative interpretation
Read Baqillani's suggestion that even if the report were sound, it could be interpreted as an expression of distress rather than an accusation.
This shows his method of giving benefit of the doubt.
5
Reflect on the methodology
Think about how Baqillani uses context, known actions, and alternative explanations to refute a weak report.
This is a model for critical evaluation of historical narrations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما رُوِيَ عن عثمان أنه كتب إلى عليّ أيام الحصار: فإن كُنْتُ مأكولاً فكن خير آكــل وإلا فادركني ولما أمزق إنما هو أيضاً من روايات الآحاد وكيف يصح ذلك، وقد أنفذ علي الحَسَن لنصرته وعثمان يرده ويرد الناس عن الدفع عنه بالقتال لهم ويحملهم الرسائل إليهم بالوعظ لهم؟ وهذا معلوم ظاهر من حاله؛ وأنه قال: «من كان يظن أن لي في عنقه طاعة فليغمد سيفه وليلزم بيت»؛ وقال لعبيده : غمد منكم سيفه فهو حر لـوجـه الله»، ففعلوا إلا الأسود الذي قتل في الدار وهذا لا يشبه ما رووه من استنهاضه لعليّ ولأن في ذلك أيضاً قرفاً لعثمان في اتهامه لمثل عليّ رضوان الله عليه في هذا الباب. فكل ما جرى هذه مجری الروايات فإنه مردود والظاهر من عليّ تكذيب هذه الرواية من قوله : «والله ما قتلتُ عثمان ولا مالات على قتله». ويمكن لو صحت هذه الرواية أن يكون هذا القول من عثمان ليس على سبيل التهمة لعلي عليه السلام بل على طريق الاستزادة في وعظ القوم وكفهم وإرساله في هذا الباب وقد يقول الإنسان مثل هذا الكلام إذا حَزَبَه الأمر وفجئه مـا يخافه على غير سبيل الظنة والتهمة .
And what is narrated from Uthman that he wrote to Ali during the days of siege: 'If I am eaten, then be the best eater, otherwise save me and do not tear me apart' — it is also from individual narrations (riwayat al-ahad). How can that be sound, while Ali had sent al-Hasan to support him, and Uthman was turning him back and turning people away from repelling [the attackers] by fighting them, and was sending messages to them with exhortation? This is well-known and evident from his situation. And he said: 'Whoever thinks that I have a right of obedience upon his neck, let him sheathe his sword and stay in his house.' And he said to his servants: 'Whoever among you sheathes his sword is free for the sake of Allah.' So they did, except al-Aswad who was killed in the house. This does not resemble what they narrated of his incitement of Ali, and because in that there is also a defamation of Uthman in accusing someone like Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, in this matter. So every narration of this sort is rejected, and the apparent [position] of Ali is the denial of this narration from his statement: 'By Allah, I did not kill Uthman nor did I incline to his killing.' And if this narration were sound, it is possible that this statement from Uthman was not by way of accusation of Ali, peace be upon him, but rather by way of seeking more exhortation of the people and restraining them, and sending [Ali] in this matter. A person may say such speech when a matter distresses him and what he fears suddenly comes upon him, not by way of suspicion and accusation.
Source pages p. 532

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a historical report concerning the siege of Uthman. The author begins by stating the report: that Uthman wrote to Ali saying a poetic line about being eaten and asking Ali to save him. He immediately declares it to be from individual narrations (riwayat al-ahad), implying it lacks the certainty required for such a serious accusation. He then provides evidence against it: Ali had sent his son al-Hasan to support Uthman, but Uthman himself turned him away and ordered people not to fight, instead sending letters of exhortation. This is well-known. Moreover, Uthman explicitly commanded his followers to sheathe swords and stay home, and freed those who complied. This contradicts the report that he sought Ali's help. The author further notes that accepting such a report would imply Uthman falsely accused Ali, which is inappropriate. Then he cites Ali's own denial: 'By Allah, I did not kill Uthman nor did I incline to his killing.' Finally, the author offers a possible interpretation if the report were sound: Uthman's words might have been out of distress, not accusation, as people sometimes say such things when overcome by fear.

Key Terms
رواية الآحاد
تكذيب الرواية
استنهاض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that any historical report is automatically reliable.
Correction: Baqillani shows how context and other known facts can refute a weak narration, even if it appears in historical records.

Checkpoint
What is Baqillani's main argument against the report that Uthman wrote to Ali?
A) The report is from individual narrations and contradicts Uthman's own orders not to fight.
B) The report is confirmed by many chains and is accepted.
C) Ali admitted that he failed to support Uthman.
D) The report is from the Quran and must be believed.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani refutes the report by showing it contradicts known historical facts and is from weak narrations, while also offering a charitable interpretation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever believed a story about someone on weak evidence, only to later discover you were wrong? How can Baqillani's method of checking contradictions and seeking alternative explanations protect you from injustice?
?
If you were in Uthman’s position, facing betrayal from those you trusted, would you be quick to accuse others or would you restrain yourself and give them the benefit of the doubt? Which path did Uthman choose according to this lesson?
?
When you hear something negative about a fellow Muslim, especially someone of known virtue, do you instinctively believe it or do you measure it against what you already know of their character and the context? Take one person you have spoken ill of recently—can you find a charitable interpretation for their action?

Why the Companions Did Not Defend Uthman
Baqillani answers the objection about why the Companions failed to defend Uthman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the theological reasons Imam Baqillani presents for why the Companions did not physically defend Uthman during the siege.

Core Idea
Obedience to Uthman's order, not cowardice, kept the Companions at home.

Imam Baqillani addresses a critical historical objection: if the attackers were unjust, why did the Companions not defend Uthman? In this passage, he explains that the Companions did not abandon Uthman; rather, they followed his explicit and repeated commands to remain at home, hoping for a peaceful resolution. This lesson unpacks Baqillani's argument and the specific examples he provides.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the passage once to grasp the structure: an objection followed by Baqillani's response. Note the strong opening denial.
Pay attention to the phrase 'معاذ الله' which signals a forceful refutation.
2
Identify the key reasons
List the reasons Baqillani gives for the Companions' inaction: Uthman's orders, hope for dispersal, expectation of reinforcements, and concern for reputation.
3
Examine the examples of Zayd and Ibn Umar
Notice how specific Companions attempted to help but were restrained by Uthman himself. This shows their willingness to fight.
Zayd's phrase 'Let us be the helpers of Allah twice' is significant.
4
Reflect on the theological implication
Consider why Baqillani argues it is impermissible to think Uthman or the Companions acted with certain knowledge of death. What would that imply?
The argument hinges on the concept of consensus (ijma) on error being impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل : فإذا كان الأمر في هذا على ما وصفتم من ظلم القوم له وتعديهم عليه فما بال الصحابة لم يسارعوا إلى إنكار ذلك وصدهم عنه؟ وأي عذر لهم في إسلامه والتساهل في خذلانه؟ قيل له : معاذ الله أن يكون فيهم خذله أو قعد عن نصرته عند دعائه لهم وإنما لزموا بيوتهم لأنه أمرهم بذلك وكرره عليهم وناشدهم الله عزّ وجلّ وعرفهم أن الجيوش توافيه وأنه لا يرى منابذة الصحابة لأهل الفتنة وإنما يجب أن يُدْفَعُوا بأمثالهم ووكد هذا القول وضيقه على القوم وقد جاء زيد بن ثابت شاكاً في سلاحه وقال له : دعنا نكن أنصار الله مرتين يعني في الدفع عنه مع الدفع عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فمنعه ذلك فأتاه بن عمر متدرّعاً فكفه طمعاً الله في أن ينصرف القوم ثانية كما انصرفوا في الأول أو في أن يلحق به من البلاد من يدفع عنه غَيْرُ الصحابة وكره أن يُتَحَدَّثَ عنه في أمصار المسلمين وغيرها أن قوما قصدوا بابه لرفع ظلامة فقتلهم وناصبهم الحرب ولقد طمع فيما يطمع فيه مِثْلُه وأحسن السيرة والتدبير في الكف والأمر بذلك . وليس يجوز أن يُعتقد فيه أنه أقعدهم عن الدفع عنه مع غلبة ظنه بأنـه يقتل لا محالة وأن القوم يقصدون نفسه دون إشكائه وإزالة الظلامة لأن ذلك من فعله لو وقع وكذلك فلا يجوز أن يُظَنَّ بالصحابة ولا بأحد منهم أنهم قعدوا عنه وتركوا الاعتراض عليه في أمره لهم بالكف مع ظنهم وتوهمهم أنه سيُقتل لأن ذلك إجماع منه ومنهم على الخطأ وإنما قدروا أن القوم ينصرفون فأطاعوه في أمره وإنما تهجموا على داره عَلَساً بسَحَرٍ ولو فعلوا ذلك بمحضر الصحابة أو بعضهم لنَدَرَتْ الرؤوس عن كواهلها دون الوصول إليه ولم يُعدّم النصرَةَ على كل حال من كافتهم أو الأكثرين منهم عدداً.
If someone says: Since the matter is as you described of the people's oppression and transgression against him, why did the Companions not hasten to denounce that and prevent them? And what excuse do they have for abandoning him and being lenient in failing to support him? It is said to him: God forbid that any of them abandoned him or sat back from supporting him when he called them. Rather, they stayed in their houses because he ordered them to do so and repeated it to them and adjured them by Allah, Mighty and Majestic, and informed them that armies would come to him, and that he did not deem it right for the Companions to confront the people of sedition, but rather that they should be repelled by their like. And he emphasized this statement and made it narrow for the people. Zayd ibn Thabit came bearing his armor and said to him: 'Let us be the helpers of Allah twice' — meaning in repelling from him along with repelling from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace — but he prevented him from that. Then Ibn Umar came to him wearing a coat of mail, and he restrained him, hoping in Allah that the people would disperse a second time as they had dispersed the first time, or that those from the towns who would repel from him other than the Companions would join him. And he disliked that it be spoken about him in the cities of the Muslims and elsewhere that people had come to his door to raise a grievance and he killed them and waged war against them. And he hoped as someone like him hopes, and he acted well in conduct and management in restraining and ordering that. And it is not permissible to believe of him that he sat them back from repelling from him while his dominant assumption was that he would inevitably be killed and that the people were aiming for his person without his complaint and removal of the grievance, because that would be an action of his if it occurred. Similarly, it is not permissible to think of the Companions or any of them that they sat back from him and left off objecting to him in his order to them to restrain, while they thought and supposed that he would be killed, because that would be a consensus from him and them upon error. Rather, they estimated that the people would disperse, so they obeyed him in his command. And indeed, they attacked his house stealthily at dawn, and if they had done that in the presence of the Companions or some of them, heads would have flown from shoulders before reaching him, and he would not have lacked support in any case from all of them or the majority of them in number.
Source pages p. 532

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer format. The objector asks: If the attackers were so unjust, why didn't the Companions defend Uthman? Baqillani responds by stating that the Companions did not abandon him; they merely obeyed Uthman's repeated and emphatic orders to stay home. Uthman hoped the besiegers would disperse again, as they had before. He also hoped for reinforcements from outside Medina, and he did not want to be seen as fighting those who came with a grievance. Baqillani gives specific examples: Zayd ibn Thabit came armed, but Uthman prevented him; Ibn Umar came in armor, but Uthman restrained him. The author then argues that it is not permissible to think that Uthman intended to leave himself unprotected while certain of death, because that would be a sinful act. Likewise, the Companions cannot be blamed because they genuinely believed the attackers would leave, so they complied. The attack happened stealthily at dawn; had the Companions known, they would have fought to the death.

Key Terms
خذلان
نصرة
الدفع
الإسلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Companions were cowardly or indifferent.
Correction: Baqillani clarifies they obeyed Uthman's orders and genuinely believed the attackers would disperse.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, why did the Companions not fight to defend Uthman?
A) They were afraid of the attackers.
B) Uthman ordered them to stay home and they expected the attackers to disperse.
C) They disapproved of Uthman's policies.
D) They were waiting for Ali to lead them.

Key Takeaway
The Companions did not abandon Uthman; they obeyed his command to stay home, hoping for a peaceful end to the siege.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When has your fear for your own safety or reputation prevented you from standing up for someone being wronged, even when that person asked you not to intervene? How does Uthman's trust in Allah and his order to the Companions challenge the way you handle fear?
?
Think of a time you obeyed a leader's instruction that seemed to put you or others at risk. Did you trust their judgment completely, or did you second-guess? How does the Companions' obedience to Uthman—despite their misgivings—push you to reexamine your own level of trust in those over you?
?
If you were in the place of Ibn Umar or Zayd ibn Thabit, would you have been able to stand down when your instinct said to fight? What does your answer reveal about your reliance on Allah's plan versus your own reasoning?

Refutation of the Claim about Uthman's Body
Baqillani rejects the claim that Uthman's body was left on a garbage heap for three days.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Baqillani refutes a historical slander against the Companions by presenting authentic reports that uphold their honor.

Core Idea
The honor of the Companions is defended by rejecting false accounts with authentic reports.

This passage directly addresses a historical claim that casts doubt on the respect shown to Caliph Uthman after his death. Baqillani firmly rejects it as a fabrication and provides the correct narrative from reliable sources, reaffirming the dignity of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the translation. Note how Baqillani starts with the claim and then refutes it.
Pay attention to the strong language: 'lie' and 'slander'.
2
Identify the two parts of Baqillani's refutation
First, he labels the claim a lie and a slander. Second, he cites the authentic reports that Uthman was buried the same day.
Notice the contrast between 'three days' and 'the same day'.
3
Reflect on the implication
Why does Baqillani stress that the true report is 'more befitting' for the Companions? This shows the importance of preserving their honor.
Consider how this refutation protects the integrity of the early community.
4
Connect to broader lessons
Think about how this passage illustrates the method of Ahl al-Sunna in defending the Companions: relying on authentic reports and rejecting fabrications.

وأما قولهم إنه بقي مُلقى على المِزْبَلَةِ ثلاثة أيام فكذب من راويه وطعن على السلف وسائر الأمة بل قد وردت الروايات أنه دفن من يــومـه وحُمِلَ من داره إلى بقيع الغَرْقَدِ؛ وهذا أظهر وأليق بمثل الصحابة. وهذا جُمَل تنبىء عن ظلم القوم وعدولهم عن الحق فيما جروا إليه .
As for their saying that he remained thrown on the garbage heap for three days — it is a lie from its narrator and a slander against the predecessors (al-salaf) and the entire community. Rather, reports have come that he was buried the same day and was carried from his house to Baqi' al-Gharqad. This is more apparent and more befitting for people like the Companions. And these are summary statements indicating the oppression of the people and their deviation from the truth in what they perpetrated.
Source pages p. 533

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a specific historical claim: that Uthman's body was left on a garbage heap for three days after his assassination. Baqillani declares this narration a lie from its narrator and a slander against the early Muslims (al-salaf) and the entire Muslim community. He then presents the authentic reports: Uthman was buried the same day and taken to the Baqi' al-Gharqad cemetery. He concludes that this version is more evident and befitting the status of the Companions. The passage ends by stating that all these points together demonstrate the injustice of the attackers and their deviation from the truth.

Key Terms
المزبلة
بقيع الغرقد
السلف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Uthman's body was left on a garbage heap for three days.
Correction: Authentic reports state he was buried the same day in Baqi' al-Gharqad.

Checkpoint
How does Baqillani describe the report that Uthman's body was left on a garbage heap?
A) It is an authentic report accepted by scholars.
B) It is a lie that slanders the early Muslims.
C) It is a possible but weak narration.
D) It is a metaphorical statement.

Key Takeaway
Imam Baqillani defends the honor of the Companions by refuting a historical slander with authentic reports.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever accepted a sensational story about a Muslim without verifying it? How might that story have harmed the person and the community in the sight of Allah? What step will you take to verify such stories from now on?
?
Baqillani says the false claim is a slander against 'the entire community' (sā'ir al-umma). Think of a time you shared gossip or a negative story about a fellow Muslim. Did you consider that you were slandering not just that person but the whole community? Will you seek forgiveness and resolve to guard your tongue?
?
When you hear a story that seems to demean the honor of the early Muslims, what is your first reaction? Do you feel a sense of duty to defend them, or do you passively let it slide? What will you do the next time you encounter such a slander in a conversation or online?

Uthman's Restraint and the Companions' Obedience
Defense of Uthman's and Companions' actions during the siege.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Uthman restrained the defenders and why the Companions obeyed him, and why it is wrong to accuse them of negligence.

Core Idea
Uthman's command was wise; the Companions obeyed expecting peace.

In this passage, Imam al-Baqillani defends the actions of Caliph Uthman and the Companions during the siege. He explains that Uthman restrained Ibn Umar and others not out of negligence but with good management, hoping the attackers would disperse. The Companions obeyed because they thought the matter would end peacefully. This lesson refutes the accusation that Uthman prevented his own defense.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the flow of the argument.
2
Identify Uthman's action and intention
Note that Uthman restrained Ibn Umar and others, hoping the attackers would disperse. Understand his reasoning.
3
Analyze the defense of the Companions
See why the author argues it is not permissible to accuse the Companions of negligence.
4
Reflect on the hypothetical scenario
Consider the author's point that if the attackers had come in the presence of many Companions, they would have been killed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من عبد دعنا نكن أنصار الله مرتين»، يعني في الدفع عنه مع الدفع عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فمنعه ذلك فأتاه بن عمر متدرّعاً فكفه طمعاً الله في أن ينصرف القوم ثانية كما انصرفوا في الأول(۱) أو في أن يلحق به من البلاد من يدفع عنه غَيْرُ الصحابة وكره أن يُتَحَدَّثَ عنه في أمصار المسلمين وغيرها أن قوما قصدوا بابه لرفع ظلامة فقتلهم وناصبهم الحرب ولقد طمع فيما يطمع فيه مِثْلُه وأحسن السيرة والتدبير في الكف والأمر بذلك . وليس يجوز أن يُعتقد فيه أنه أقعدهم عن الدفع عنه مع غلبة ظنه بأنـه يقتل لا محالة وأن القوم يقصدون نفسه دون إشكائه وإزالة الظلامة لأن ذلك من فعله لو وقع وكذلك فلا يجوز أن يُظَنَّ بالصحابة ولا بأحد منهم أنهم قعدوا عنه وتركوا الاعتراض عليه في أمره لهم بالكف مع ظنهم وتوهمهم أنه سيُقتل لأن ذلك إجماع منه ومنهم على الخطأ وإنما قدروا أن القوم ينصرفون فأطاعوه في أمره وإنما تهجموا على داره عَلَساً بسَحَرٍ ولو فعلوا ذلك بمحضر الصحابة أو بعضهم لنَدَرَتْ الرؤوس عن كواهلها دون الوصول إليه ولم يُعدّم النصرَةَ على كل حال من كافتهم أو الأكثرين منهم عدداً.
وأما قولهم إنه بقي مُلقى على المِزْبَلَةِ ثلاثة أيام فكذب من راويه وطعن على السلف وسائر الأمة بل قد وردت الروايات أنه دفن من يــومـه وحُمِلَ من داره إلى بقيع الغَرْقَدِ(۲) ؛ وهذا أظهر وأليق بمثل الصحابة. وهذا جُمَل تنبىء عن ظلم القوم وعدولهم عن الحق فيما جروا إليه .
From 'abd (servant) [said]: 'Let us be the helpers of God twice,' meaning in repelling him along with repelling the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace. So that prevented him, and Ibn Umar came wearing armor and restrained him, hoping that the people would turn away a second time as they had turned away the first time, or that those who would repel him from the lands would join him, other than the Companions, and he disliked that it be spoken about him in the cities of the Muslims and elsewhere that a group had come to his door to raise a grievance and he killed them and fought them. And he hoped for what someone like him hopes for, and he had the best conduct and management in restraining and commanding that. And it is not permissible to believe of him that he incapacitated them from repelling him despite his strong belief that he would inevitably be killed and that the group intended him personally, not his injuries or removal of the grievance, because that would be from his action if it occurred. Likewise, it is not permissible to think of the Companions or any of them that they held back from him and left off objecting to his command to them to restrain, despite their thinking and assumption that he would be killed, because that would be a consensus from him and them on error. Rather, they thought that the people would turn away, so they obeyed him in his command. And they only assaulted his house stealthily at dawn. And if they had done that in the presence of the Companions or some of them, heads would have flown from their shoulders without reaching him, and he would not have lacked victory in any case from all of them or the majority of them in number. As for their saying that he remained thrown on a garbage dump for three days, it is a lie from its narrator and an attack on the Salaf and the entire Ummah. Rather, reports have come that he was buried on the same day and carried from his house to Baqi' al-Gharqad(۲). This is more apparent and more befitting of the likes of the Companions. And this is a summary that indicates the oppression of the people and their deviation from the truth in what they perpetrated.
Source pages p. 533

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the actions of the Companions during the siege of Caliph Uthman's house. The author first explains the context: a group of people came to Uthman's door with a grievance, and Uthman, hoping they would disperse, restrained Ibn Umar from fighting them. The author argues that Uthman acted with good management, and it is wrong to think that he intentionally left the Companions unable to defend him. Then the author refutes the claim that the Companions abandoned him; rather, they obeyed his command because they thought the attackers would leave. The author further states that if the attackers had come in the presence of many Companions, they would have been killed. Finally, the author directly refutes the accusation that Uthman was left on a garbage dump for three days, calling it a lie and an attack on the early generations, citing reports that he was buried the same day in Baqi' al-Gharqad. This shows the injustice of the attackers.

Key Terms
الصحابة
إجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Companions abandoned Uthman out of cowardice or negligence.
Correction: The Companions obeyed Uthman's command to restrain, expecting the attackers to disperse peacefully.

Checkpoint
Why did the Companions obey Uthman's command to restrain according to the passage?
A) They were cowardly and wanted to avoid fighting.
B) They thought the attackers would turn away and leave peacefully.
C) They wanted Uthman to be killed.
D) They were forced by Uthman.

Key Takeaway
Uthman's restraint was a calculated decision, and the Companions' obedience was based on reasonable hope, not neglect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are in a position of authority, do you prioritize avoiding conflict even when it might cost you personally? Are you willing to risk misunderstanding or martyrdom for the sake of peace, as Uthman did?
?
Have you ever obeyed a leader's command even when you feared it might lead to harm? What does that say about your trust in Allah's plan versus your own assessment of danger?
?
If you were among the Companions, would you have questioned Uthman's order or trusted his judgment? How does your answer reveal the state of your heart regarding obedience to legitimate authority in difficult times?

Refuting the Garbage Dump Claim
Direct refutation of the garbage dump accusation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claim that Uthman was left on a garbage dump for three days is false and an attack on the Salaf.

Core Idea
The claim is a lie; Uthman was buried the same day in Baqi'.

This passage directly addresses a slanderous accusation against the Companions: that they left Caliph Uthman's body on a garbage dump for three days. Imam al-Baqillani declares this a lie and an attack on the entire early Muslim community. He cites reports that Uthman was buried on the same day in the Baqi' cemetery, a fact befitting the Companions' honor.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to see the direct denial of the claim.
2
Note the author's condemnation
The author calls the claim a lie and an attack on the Salaf and the entire Ummah.
3
Find the evidence
The passage mentions that Uthman was buried the same day in Baqi' al-Gharqad.
4
Understand the implication
This refutation shows the injustice of the attackers and defends the honor of the Companions.

Refuting General Accusations Against Uthman
Dismissal of accusations and introduction of interpretative principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author dismisses the accusations against Uthman as baseless and establishes the principle of interpreting a ruler's actions as sound.

Core Idea
Even if accusations were true, Uthman's actions must be interpreted as correct.

The author begins by listing the specific accusations against Uthman—beating Ammar and Ibn Mas'ud, withholding stipends. He immediately declares them false according to many, lacking evidence. More importantly, he introduces a key principle: even if such actions were proven, they must be understood as sound and justified given Uthman's position.

Guided Path
1
Read the accusations
Read the Arabic and translation listing what the opponents claimed Uthman did. Notice the severity of the alleged acts.
2
Identify the author's response
The author says the reports are false and not substantiated by evidence. He also adds a conditional argument.
Focus on 'فباطل عند كثير من الناس' and the phrase 'لو ثبت ذلك'.
3
Understand the principle
Even if proven, the action must be 'carried upon correctness'—a foundational rule in defending the Companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ذكر ما تعلقوا به على عثمان ونقموا من فعله والجواب عنه
فأما تعلقهم بأنه ضرب عَمّاراً حتى فتق أمعاءه (۱) وضرب عبد الله أضلاعه ومنعه العطاء سنين كثيرة وأنه رد عليه مسعود حتى كسر ضلعين من عطاءه (۲) فباطل عند كثير من الناس وليس ما يروون في هذا مما نُضْطَرُّ إليه أو مما قام دليل عليه ولا مما يُثبت تعلق القوم به. وعلى أنه لو ثبت ذلك، لوجب أن يحمل فعله على الصحة (۳) وقد رُوي أن سبب ضربه لعمار أنه قال للطاعنين عليه اكتبوا ما تشكونه من عثمان في كتاب واعطونيه حتى أدخل عليه وأوقفه عليه، فكتب ذلك ودخل عليه فغلّظ له في القول وافترى واستخف بسلطان الله وليس له ذلك، ولا يحل له ولا لغيره أن يخاطب عثمان بذلك؛ وليس بأمير المؤمنين إلا بما يقتضيه ما ذكرناه من محله في الدين ومنزلته بين المسلمين وحرمته وسابقته في الدين فكيف وهو السلطان المأمور بطاعته وترك الافتيات عليه؟ وليس فيما أنكروه عليه مُنكَر يستحق به مثل ما خرج إليه عمار .
وقد رُوي أنه كان يقول: عثمان كافر؛ وكان يقول بعد قتله : قتلنا عثمان يوم قتلناه كافراً حتى قال له علي عليه السلام مرة وهو
(۳) قال المحب الطبري في الرياض النضرة ۹۲/۳ ما نصه : وأما القضية الثالثة وهو ما ادعوه من بن مسعود فكان ذلك في مقابلة ما بلغه عنه تزل الأئمة على مثل ذلك، وكل منهما مجتهد، فإما مصيبان أو مخطىء ،ومصيب، ولم يكن قصد عثمان حرمانه البتة، وإنما التأخير إلى غاية اقتضى نظره التأخير إليها أدباً، فلما قضى عليه إما مع بلوغ حصول تلك الغاية أو دونها وصل به ورثته، ولعله كان أنفع لهم ثم عقب في صحيفة ٩٥ قائلاً وأما القضية العاشرة ما رووه مما جرى على عبد الله بن مسعود من عثمان وأمره غلامه بضربه إلى آخر ما قرروه فكله بهتان واختلاق لا يصح منه شيء وهؤلاء الجهلة لا يتحامون الكذب فيما يرونه موافقاً لأغراضهم، إذا ديانة تردهم عن ذلك.
Chapter: Mentioning what they used against Uthman and criticized from his action, and the response about it.
As for their claim that he beat Ammar until he split his intestines, and beat Abdullah (ibn Mas'ud) on his ribs and prevented his stipend for many years, and that he responded to him (i.e., refused him) until he broke two ribs from his stipend, it is false according to many people. What they narrate about this is not something we are forced to accept, nor is there evidence for it, nor does it prove their claim. Even if it were proven, it would be necessary to interpret his action as sound. And it has been reported that the reason for his beating Ammar was that he (Ammar) said to those criticizing Uthman: 'Write what you complain about Uthman in a book and give it to me so that I may enter upon him and inform him of it.' So they wrote that, and he entered upon him and spoke harshly to him, slandered him, and belittled the authority of God—he has no right to do that, nor is it permissible for him or anyone else to address Uthman in that manner. He is not the Commander of the Faithful except by what we have mentioned of his standing in religion, his rank among the Muslims, his sanctity, and his precedence in religion. So how (can he do that) when he is the ruler commanded to be obeyed and not to be opposed? There is nothing in what they objected to him that is an evil deserving what Ammar did to him. And it has been reported that Ammar used to say: 'Uthman is an infidel,' and he used to say after his killing: 'We killed Uthman on the day we killed him while he was an infidel,' until Ali, peace be upon him, said to him once...
(3) Al-Muhibb al-Tabari said in al-Riyad al-Nadira 3/92, verbatim: 'As for the third case, which is what they claimed regarding Ibn Mas'ud, that was in response to what reached him (Uthman) about (Ibn Mas'ud) destabilizing the leaders over such matters—each of them is a mujtahid, either both are correct or one is mistaken and one correct. Uthman did not intend to deprive him absolutely; rather, the delay was until a point that his judgment required delay for discipline. When it came to pass, either with the attainment of that point or before, he gave it to his heirs, and perhaps that was more beneficial for them. Then he followed up on page 95 saying: 'As for the tenth case, what they narrated about what happened to Abdullah ibn Mas'ud from Uthman and his ordering his slave to beat him, etc., all of it is falsehood and fabrication—nothing of it is authentic. These ignorant people do not refrain from lying when they see it supporting their desires, even if religion would deter them from that.'
Source pages p. 534

Commentary
This passage is a chapter heading and refutation of specific accusations against Caliph Uthman. The author begins by stating the accusations: that Uthman beat Ammar until his intestines prolapsed, beat Ibn Mas'ud and broke his ribs, and withheld his stipend. The author dismisses these as false according to many people, lacking evidence. Even if proven, they must be interpreted as sound actions. Then the author provides a reported reason for beating Ammar: Ammar acted improperly by entering upon Uthman with harsh words and slander, which justifies the punishment, given Uthman's high status as ruler. The author adds that Ammar went further by calling Uthman an infidel, even after his death. The passage then includes a long quotation from al-Muhibb al-Tabari defending Uthman's handling of Ibn Mas'ud, arguing that Uthman's delay of the stipend was a discretionary discipline and that the claim of beating is entirely fabricated. The overall argument is that the opponents of Uthman spread lies, and even if true, the actions would be justified.

Key Terms

عمار
ابن مسعود
باطل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The accusations against Uthman are proven and show he wronged these companions.
Correction: The author argues the accusations are baseless and even if proven, Uthman's actions must be assumed correct due to his righteous status.

Checkpoint
What is the author's main argument if the accusations against Uthman were proven true?
A) Uthman should be condemned
B) Uthman's actions must be interpreted as sound
C) The accusations were exaggerated
D) Uthman apologized later

Key Takeaway
The accusations are dismissed as unsubstantiated, and even if true, Uthman's actions are to be seen as correct.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear negative stories about someone you respect, do you immediately doubt them or do you demand solid evidence? How does this lesson's emphasis on 'no evidence' challenge your own habits?
?
If you were in Uthman's position and someone falsely accused you, would you hope for people to give you the benefit of the doubt? Are you willing to extend that same grace to others, especially leaders you may disagree with?
?
This lesson says even if accusations were true, we must interpret the action as correct. In your own life, is there a person you have judged harshly? Can you now rethink that situation and assume the best motive?

Justification for Beating Ammar
Narrative justification for Uthman's punishment of Ammar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reported reason for Uthman's beating of Ammar and how it justifies the punishment.

Core Idea
Ammar's disrespectful conduct justified Uthman's disciplinary action.

After dismissing the general accusations, the author provides a specific reported cause for the beating of Ammar. According to this narration, Ammar instigated the complainants to write down their grievances, then entered upon Uthman with harsh words and slander, which warranted a response. The author emphasizes that such behavior is unacceptable toward a ruler of Uthman's stature.

Guided Path
1
Read the reported cause
Read the Arabic and translation describing how Ammar asked for written complaints and then confronted Uthman harshly.
Notice the phrase 'فغلّظ له في القول وافترى'.
2
Identify the justification
The author explains that Ammar's actions were impermissible: he belittled the authority of God and disrespected the caliph.
Focus on 'لا يحل له ولا لغيره أن يخاطب عثمان بذلك'.
3
Consider Uthman's status
The passage highlights Uthman's high rank in religion, precedence, and his position as the ruler whose obedience is commanded.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ذكر ما تعلقوا به على عثمان ونقموا من فعله والجواب عنه
فأما تعلقهم بأنه ضرب عَمّاراً حتى فتق أمعاءه (۱) وضرب عبد الله أضلاعه ومنعه العطاء سنين كثيرة وأنه رد عليه مسعود حتى كسر ضلعين من عطاءه (۲) فباطل عند كثير من الناس وليس ما يروون في هذا مما نُضْطَرُّ إليه أو مما قام دليل عليه ولا مما يُثبت تعلق القوم به. وعلى أنه لو ثبت ذلك، لوجب أن يحمل فعله على الصحة (۳) وقد رُوي أن سبب ضربه لعمار أنه قال للطاعنين عليه اكتبوا ما تشكونه من عثمان في كتاب واعطونيه حتى أدخل عليه وأوقفه عليه، فكتب ذلك ودخل عليه فغلّظ له في القول وافترى واستخف بسلطان الله وليس له ذلك، ولا يحل له ولا لغيره أن يخاطب عثمان بذلك؛ وليس بأمير المؤمنين إلا بما يقتضيه ما ذكرناه من محله في الدين ومنزلته بين المسلمين وحرمته وسابقته في الدين فكيف وهو السلطان المأمور بطاعته وترك الافتيات عليه؟ وليس فيما أنكروه عليه مُنكَر يستحق به مثل ما خرج إليه عمار .
وقد رُوي أنه كان يقول: عثمان كافر؛ وكان يقول بعد قتله : قتلنا عثمان يوم قتلناه كافراً حتى قال له علي عليه السلام مرة وهو
(۳) قال المحب الطبري في الرياض النضرة ۹۲/۳ ما نصه : وأما القضية الثالثة وهو ما ادعوه من بن مسعود فكان ذلك في مقابلة ما بلغه عنه تزل الأئمة على مثل ذلك، وكل منهما مجتهد، فإما مصيبان أو مخطىء ،ومصيب، ولم يكن قصد عثمان حرمانه البتة، وإنما التأخير إلى غاية اقتضى نظره التأخير إليها أدباً، فلما قضى عليه إما مع بلوغ حصول تلك الغاية أو دونها وصل به ورثته، ولعله كان أنفع لهم ثم عقب في صحيفة ٩٥ قائلاً وأما القضية العاشرة ما رووه مما جرى على عبد الله بن مسعود من عثمان وأمره غلامه بضربه إلى آخر ما قرروه فكله بهتان واختلاق لا يصح منه شيء وهؤلاء الجهلة لا يتحامون الكذب فيما يرونه موافقاً لأغراضهم، إذا ديانة تردهم عن ذلك.
Chapter: Mentioning what they used against Uthman and criticized from his action, and the response about it.
As for their claim that he beat Ammar until he split his intestines, and beat Abdullah (ibn Mas'ud) on his ribs and prevented his stipend for many years, and that he responded to him (i.e., refused him) until he broke two ribs from his stipend, it is false according to many people. What they narrate about this is not something we are forced to accept, nor is there evidence for it, nor does it prove their claim. Even if it were proven, it would be necessary to interpret his action as sound. And it has been reported that the reason for his beating Ammar was that he (Ammar) said to those criticizing Uthman: 'Write what you complain about Uthman in a book and give it to me so that I may enter upon him and inform him of it.' So they wrote that, and he entered upon him and spoke harshly to him, slandered him, and belittled the authority of God—he has no right to do that, nor is it permissible for him or anyone else to address Uthman in that manner. He is not the Commander of the Faithful except by what we have mentioned of his standing in religion, his rank among the Muslims, his sanctity, and his precedence in religion. So how (can he do that) when he is the ruler commanded to be obeyed and not to be opposed? There is nothing in what they objected to him that is an evil deserving what Ammar did to him. And it has been reported that Ammar used to say: 'Uthman is an infidel,' and he used to say after his killing: 'We killed Uthman on the day we killed him while he was an infidel,' until Ali, peace be upon him, said to him once...
(3) Al-Muhibb al-Tabari said in al-Riyad al-Nadira 3/92, verbatim: 'As for the third case, which is what they claimed regarding Ibn Mas'ud, that was in response to what reached him (Uthman) about (Ibn Mas'ud) destabilizing the leaders over such matters—each of them is a mujtahid, either both are correct or one is mistaken and one correct. Uthman did not intend to deprive him absolutely; rather, the delay was until a point that his judgment required delay for discipline. When it came to pass, either with the attainment of that point or before, he gave it to his heirs, and perhaps that was more beneficial for them. Then he followed up on page 95 saying: 'As for the tenth case, what they narrated about what happened to Abdullah ibn Mas'ud from Uthman and his ordering his slave to beat him, etc., all of it is falsehood and fabrication—nothing of it is authentic. These ignorant people do not refrain from lying when they see it supporting their desires, even if religion would deter them from that.'
Source pages p. 534

Commentary
This passage is a chapter heading and refutation of specific accusations against Caliph Uthman. The author begins by stating the accusations: that Uthman beat Ammar until his intestines prolapsed, beat Ibn Mas'ud and broke his ribs, and withheld his stipend. The author dismisses these as false according to many people, lacking evidence. Even if proven, they must be interpreted as sound actions. Then the author provides a reported reason for beating Ammar: Ammar acted improperly by entering upon Uthman with harsh words and slander, which justifies the punishment, given Uthman's high status as ruler. The author adds that Ammar went further by calling Uthman an infidel, even after his death. The passage then includes a long quotation from al-Muhibb al-Tabari defending Uthman's handling of Ibn Mas'ud, arguing that Uthman's delay of the stipend was a discretionary discipline and that the claim of beating is entirely fabricated. The overall argument is that the opponents of Uthman spread lies, and even if true, the actions would be justified.

Key Terms
عمار
عثمان
افتيات
سلطان الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Uthman beat Ammar without just cause, showing tyranny.
Correction: The reported cause shows Ammar was at fault: he spoke harshly and belittled the ruler, which warranted punishment.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did Ammar do that led to his beating?
A) He refused to pay zakat
B) He led a rebellion
C) He entered upon Uthman with harsh speech and slander
D) He stole from the treasury

Key Takeaway
Ammar's disrespectful behavior justified Uthman's disciplinary action.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have heard that Ammar, a great companion, was beaten. Now read the justification: he belittled God's authority. Have you ever spoken harshly to a parent, teacher, or leader, thinking you were right? What will you do the next time you feel anger toward someone in authority over you?
?
The author says Uthman's rank in religion and sanctity made such treatment impermissible. There is someone in your life whom God has placed in authority over you—perhaps a parent, a spouse, or a community leader. Do you truly honor their position as a trust from God, or do you allow your own opinions to justify disrespect? What one step can you take today to correct this?
?
Ammar's intention was to convey complaints, but his method was condemned. You too may have good intentions when you correct others. But ask yourself: Are you doing it with the adab (respect) that Islam demands? Or do you assume the end justifies the means? How will you change your approach starting now?

Refuting Claims About Ibn Mas'ud
Refutation of accusations concerning Ibn Mas'ud, citing al-Tabari's detailed defense.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes claims about Uthman's mistreatment of Ibn Mas'ud, including the al-Tabari quotation that declares the reports fabrications.

Core Idea
The claims about Ibn Mas'ud are lies; Uthman's actions were disciplinary and later compensated.

The passage continues with further reports about Ammar calling Uthman an infidel and then a lengthy quotation from al-Muhibb al-Tabari's 'al-Riyad al-Nadira.' Al-Tabari addresses two cases: the third (Ibn Mas'ud's stipend delay) and the tenth (the alleged beating). He argues that Uthman acted as a disciplinarian, both were mujtahids, and the beating story is pure fabrication.

Guided Path
1
Read the report about Ammar's extreme statements
Notice that Ammar called Uthman an infidel both before and after his death. This sets context for the bias of the accusers.
2
Analyze al-Tabari's first case (Ibn Mas'ud's stipend)
Al-Tabari explains the delay was a discretionary discipline, not deprivation, and Uthman eventually gave the stipend to his heirs.
Focus on 'لم يكن قصد عثمان حرمانه البتة'.
3
Analyze al-Tabari's tenth case (the beating)
Al-Tabari declares this report 'falsehood and fabrication' and criticizes the narrators as ignorant liars.
Note the strong language: 'كله بهتان واختلاق'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Al-Tabari dismisses the beating reports as 'falsehood and fabrication' from ignorant liars driven by their desires. In your own life, have you ever accepted a story against someone because it suited your pre-existing opinion? What would it take for you to verify such reports before believing them?
?
