Defense of Uthman's Appointment of Relatives
Baqillani refutes the claim that Uthman's appointments of relatives were improper.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument that Uthman's appointments of relatives were justified by the qualifications of the appointees and the lack of proven sinfulness.

Core Idea
Qualifications, not relation, determine the validity of appointments.

In this passage, Imam al-Baqillani addresses the accusation that Caliph Uthman appointed his relatives improperly. He argues that the critics have no basis unless they can prove the appointees were sinners and that Uthman knew of their sin. Instead, Baqillani highlights that these individuals were capable and even served under Umar without criticism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand Baqillani's line of reasoning.
Pay attention to the conditional argument.
2
Identify the condition
Notice that Baqillani sets a condition for accepting the criticism: the critics must prove moral corruption and Uthman's knowledge.
3
Consider the counter-evidence
Baqillani offers evidence of the appointees' qualifications and Mu'awiya's service under Umar.
This shifts the burden of proof.
4
Reflect on the principle
Think about the broader principle: appointments are judged by capability, not by family ties.
This relates to Islamic governance ethics.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما تعلقوا به من تولية أقاربه كمعاوية وعبد الرحمن بن عثمان ومروان بن الحكم وغيرهم، فلا متعلق فيه دون أن يُثبتوا أنهم فساق وأن فسقهم ثبت عند عثمان فأقرهم وأنه ولاهم يوم ولاهم وهم فساق ليسوا بأهل الولاية وقد كان هؤلاء النفر أهل نجدة وكفاية وبصَر بالإمرة وقدرة عليها وإن لم يكونوا زهاداً وقد كان معاوية من أمراء عمر طول مدته فمـا نقـم عليـه أحد .
As for what they have clung to concerning his appointment of his relatives such as Mu'awiya, Abd al-Rahman ibn Uthman, Marwan ibn al-Hakam, and others, there is no basis in it unless they prove that they were sinners and that their sinfulness was established before Uthman yet he retained them, and that he appointed them at the time of appointment while they were sinners, not fit for governorship. Yet these individuals were people of bravery, capability, insight into command, and ability for it, even if they were not ascetics. And Mu'awiya was one of Umar's governors throughout his tenure, and no one criticized him.
Source pages p. 542

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the accusation that Uthman improperly appointed relatives. Baqillani argues that the critics must first prove that the appointees were sinners and that Uthman knew of their sin yet kept them in office. He then asserts that the appointees were actually qualified—brave, capable, and insightful—even if not ascetics. He specifically notes that Mu'awiya served under Umar without criticism, implying that the same appointment was legitimate under Uthman.

Key Terms
تولية الأقارب (appointment of relatives)
فساق (sinners)
أهل نجدة (people of bravery)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Uthman's appointment of relatives was inherently unjust nepotism.
Correction: Baqillani argues that the appointments are justified if the appointees are qualified and not proven sinners, regardless of family ties.

Checkpoint
What condition does Baqillani set before accepting the criticism of Uthman's appointments?
A) That the appointees were not ascetics
B) That the critics were also qualified
C) That the appointees were proven sinners in Uthman's knowledge
D) That the appointments were not from the caliph's family

Key Takeaway
Baqillani defends Uthman's appointments by arguing that critics must prove the appointees were sinners and that Uthman knowingly appointed them, while highlighting their qualifications and prior service.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you evaluate a leader or an appointment, do you focus on their relationship to you or on their actual qualifications? Where in your life are you most prone to assume bias without proof, just as the critics assumed about Uthman?
?
Uthman's appointees were not ascetics, but they were capable. Have you ever dismissed someone's leadership because they didn't fit your ideal of religious devotion, while ignoring their competence? How does this lesson challenge your criteria for leadership?
?
Baqillani demands evidence before accepting criticism. What criticism are you currently holding against someone without checking the facts? Will you commit to seeking proof before condemning, even if it means changing your opinion?

Defense of Uthman Against Favoritism Accusations
Baqillani refutes the claim that Uthman favored relatives with wealth from the treasury.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani refutes the accusation that Uthman favored relatives with wealth from the treasury, and how he defends Uthman's integrity.

Core Idea
Baqillani defends Uthman's piety and generosity, dismissing accusations as unproven.

Baqillani addresses a sensitive accusation against Caliph Uthman, that he gave preferential treatment and wealth to his relatives. In this passage, he firmly rejects the claim as false and explains Uthman's character and the weakness of the evidence. This lesson explores Baqillani's method of defense and the principles behind it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then the literal translation. Let the author's own words come through before analysis.
The passage is a direct refutation of a specific accusation.
2
Identify the main accusation
Find what the opponents claimed about Uthman's treatment of relatives. The passage mentions love, special gifts, and giving the fifth of Ifriqiya to Marwan.
The fifth of Ifriqiya was a significant amount of war spoils.
3
Observe Baqillani's counter-arguments
Notice how Baqillani first calls the accusation false, then describes Uthman's piety and generosity. He also addresses the story of borrowing from the treasury.
Baqillani emphasizes Uthman's personal wealth and God-consciousness.
4
Analyze the borrowing story
Understand why Baqillani dismisses the story that Uthman borrowed from the treasury. He argues it is weak because Uthman was wealthy enough not to need to borrow.
The principle: an accusation unproven is not to be accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قولهم إنه كان يحبهم ويخصهم بالعطاء وإنه أعطى مروان جميع خُمس إفريقية فإنه باطل وتوهم منهم وقد كان عثمان أتقى الله وأنْزَة نفساً مع إنفاقه في سبيل الله وكثرة بذله لماله ونفسه في نُصرَةِ الدين. وقد ذُكر أنه إنما أعطى من مال نفسه وقال لهم مرة في قسمه : «إنما اقترضت من بيت مال المسلمين؛ وهذا ضعيف؛ لأنه كان غير محتاج إلى اقتراض مع سعة ماله؛ ومتى لم يثبت عليه ذلك، لم يحل قرفه به.
As for their saying that he loved them and singled them out with gifts, and that he gave Marwan all of the fifth of Ifriqiya, it is false and a delusion from them. Uthman was more God-fearing and dignified in soul, with his spending in the way of God and his great expenditure of his wealth and soul in support of the religion. And it has been mentioned that he only gave from his own wealth, and he said to them once in his division: 'I only borrowed from the treasury of the Muslims'; and this is weak, because he was not in need of borrowing given his ample wealth; and as long as that is not proven against him, it is not permissible to accuse him with it.
Source pages p. 543

Commentary
This passage defends Uthman against the accusation that he gave Marwan the entire fifth of the spoils of Ifriqiya. Baqillani calls this accusation false and a delusion. He describes Uthman as pious and generous with his own wealth for the sake of religion. He then addresses the story that Uthman claimed he borrowed from the treasury, dismissing it as weak because Uthman was wealthy enough not to need to borrow. Since the accusation is unproven, it is impermissible to accuse him of wrongdoing.

Key Terms
خمس إفريقية (fifth of Ifriqiya)
اقتراض (borrowing)
بيت مال المسلمين (treasury of the Muslims)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim that Uthman borrowed from the treasury to give gifts, implying financial impropriety.
Correction: Baqillani shows this claim is weak because Uthman was personally wealthy and would not need to borrow, and the accusation is unproven.

Checkpoint
Why does Baqillani dismiss the claim that Uthman borrowed from the treasury to give gifts?
A) Because Uthman never borrowed anything
B) Because Uthman was wealthy and had no need to borrow
C) Because the treasury was empty
D) Because Marwan refused the gift

Key Takeaway
Baqillani rejects the accusation against Uthman as false and unproven, emphasizing his piety and wealth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a negative story about someone you know, do you instinctively believe it or question it? How can you apply Baqillani's standard of proof—'as long as it is not proven, it is not permissible to accuse'—to your own thoughts and speech?
?
Uthman was wealthy and generous, yet still accused of favoritism. Is there someone in your life whom you have misjudged based on incomplete information? What would it take for you to defend them as Baqillani defended Uthman?
?
Are you more like those who spread accusations or like Baqillani who demands evidence before making a judgment? This lesson requires you to examine your own habits: will you commit to verifying every negative claim before accepting or repeating it?

Baqillani's Defense of Uthman's Disciplinary Methods
Baqillani justifies Uthman's escalation from whip to stick in disciplining companions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's defense of Uthman's disciplinary escalation as a legitimate exercise of the imam's authority.

Core Idea
The imam has wide discretion in discipline; Uthman's stick was within his rights.

This passage addresses a specific criticism leveled against Uthman: that he exceeded proper limits by using a stick instead of a whip on Companions. Baqillani counters by grounding the imam's authority to choose disciplinary measures, sparing no detail about the range of options available. The lesson shows how classical theologians defended the actions of the Companions against sectarian objections.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then its literal translation. Let the objection and response unfold naturally.
Pay attention to the specific terms for whip (الدرة) and stick (العصا).
2
Identify the objection
Notice that critics, including Aisha, objected to Uthman's escalation from whip to stick. This is the point Baqillani must answer.
3
Understand Baqillani's response
Baqillani argues that the imam has inherent authority to choose whatever method of discipline he deems fit, including the stick. He lists multiple options to show the scope of that authority.
The phrase 'لا عتب عليه' (no blame on him) is key.
4
Note the rhetorical move
Baqillani strengthens his case by saying even Umar would have used the stick if needed, implying the method is not inherently improper.
This appeals to the consensus of the early community.
5
Reflect on the broader principle
The imam's discretionary authority in discipline is not unlimited but is broad enough to cover measures like the stick, provided they serve the purpose of correction.
This reflects the Sunni view of the imam's role in maintaining order.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما تعلقهم بما أنكرته عائشة وغيرها من تجاوزه في تأديب الصحابة الضربَ بالدّرِّةِ إلى الضرب بالعصا فلا عتب عليه في ذلك لأن للإمام التقويم والضرب بالدّرّةِ والضرب من الواحد إلى الألف مرة بالعصا ومرة بالدرة ومرة بالانتهار والقول ولو أن عمر احتاج معهم إلى العصا لفعل.
As for their clinging to what Aisha and others objected to, namely his going beyond in disciplining the Companions from beating with the whip to beating with the stick, there is no blame on him in that, because the imam has the authority to correct and beat with the whip, and beating from one to a thousand times with the stick, and sometimes with the whip, and sometimes with rebuke and words. And if Umar had needed with them the stick, he would have done it.
Source pages p. 543

Commentary
This passage defends Uthman's use of a stick instead of the traditional whip for disciplining some Companions. Baqillani argues that the imam has the right to choose the appropriate punishment, including beating with a stick up to a thousand times, or using the whip, verbal rebuke, or words. He even notes that Umar would have used the stick if necessary, implying that the method itself is not inherently wrong.

Key Terms
التأديب (discipline)
الدرة (whip)
العصا (stick)
الإمام (the imam)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Uthman's use of the stick was an excessive innovation in discipline.
Correction: Baqillani argues that the imam has the authority to determine the method and intensity of discipline, so Uthman's action was legitimate.

Checkpoint
What is the basis for Baqillani's defense of Uthman's use of the stick?
A) Uthman had permission from Aisha
B) The imam has authority to choose disciplinary methods
C) The stick is less painful than the whip
D) Umar had also used a stick

Key Takeaway
The imam has discretionary authority to choose disciplinary methods, so Uthman's escalation to the stick was justified.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear criticism of a leader's actions, do you rush to judgment or consider the scope of their authority? How does this passage challenge your tendency to assume you know better than the imam? Will you pause before judging religious authorities in the future?
?
The imam has discretion to discipline even Companions. Do you accept that religious authority includes the right to use physical punishment? How does your modern sensitivity conflict with this teaching? Can you submit to it despite its discomfort?
?
Baqillani says 'there is no blame on him.' Is there a leader in your life whom you have blamed unfairly? Will you ask Allah to forgive your presumptuousness and repent from speaking ill of those in authority?
